Nantong 72

Urgently Build the Wanggang Embankment's Perilous Section: The Jiang'an coast near Nantong's Wanggang is experiencing severe erosion, posing an extreme danger. The Construction Bureau, recognizing that the Linchao and other villages have already suffered tidal disasters, held an emergency meeting of representatives from all sectors and decided that the county government should immediately issue a notice to solicit labor and urgently build the embankment. It is proposed to levy a donation of 3.5 li per mu of land to secure the embankment against collapse and requested the Construction Department to approve it immediately.

Banditry Rampant in Various Districts in Eastern Township: In recent days, gangs of bandits numbering two to three thousand have gathered in various districts in Nantong's eastern township, causing riots. The county police squad stationed there has been surrounded and has lost all ammunition. Businessmen and residents have evacuated the Siyangba area. The bandits have set up a fake command post at the Wufuqiao in Dongshe, ordering the people to hang red flags. The 15th squadron of the Provincial Police Team has arrived from the province and is rushing to Erjia Town. Commander Xiong from Songhu sent a regiment to Tong on the 25th. The bandits in the eastern township have not yet harassed the people too much. Yu Donglai, the head of the town urgently informed the Nantong emergency meeting, recounted the absurd and erroneous actions of Yan Diannan, the captain of the county police squad, and reported that he had sold guns and ammunition to the bandits. The delegates were outraged and jointly submitted a petition to the province and county, demanding a thorough investigation. Recently, the security of the city remains under the responsibility of the Marine Corps. It is reported that after the bandits seized the firearms from the county police squad, they surrounded and searched the Siyangba Public Security Bureau and the Yiyu District Office, abducting more than ten officials, including Ling Xiao, who was an assistant at the district office. Due to being hated by the bandits, Ling's limbs were cut off in public, his head was severed, and his chest was cut open, and his heart was cooked and eaten. All the other captured people were released. Ling's head is still hanging on a power pole in the town.

Expedite the Joint Defense of Six Counties: The Department of Civil Affairs ordered that the bandit suppression affairs of Nantong, Taixian, Rugao, Jingjiang, and Taixing counties be incorporated into the joint defense plan of Nantong, Taizhou, Rugao, Jingjiang, Taidong, and Taizhou counties. It has now issued an order to expedite the process and set a date for implementation.

Rugao 73

Police Squad in Jiangjiazhuang Suppresses Bandits: At around 10:00 PM on the 22nd, many bandits were suddenly discovered in Jiangjiazhuang, about five li from the city. They used flashlights and then opened fire, attempting to attack the Second Police Outpost of the Third Branch Station. The stationed police received the information and returned fire. The engagement lasted for about an hour. Meanwhile, personnel were dispatched to report in all directions. The Public Security Bureau and the Provincial Police Team dispatched teams in succession for reinforcements. At the same time, Xie, the Provincial Police Team's deputy corps leader, sent two machine gun companies to set up secret defenses from the Second Yang Bridge in the east to the Yang Bridge outside the West Gate and to the Sanjie Bridge in the south. Inside the city, the Protection Corps and police stepped up security. After the teams reached Pingxiang in the morning, the bandits had been repelled by 5:00 AM, and the teams returned to the city. Today (the 23rd), the city imposed a curfew early. The Provincial Party Headquarters sent personnel to investigate the case. Xu Shencun, a staff member of the Organization Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters, came to Rugao the day before yesterday to investigate a certain case and is currently conducting investigations in all directions.

Dispatch Troops to Juegang to Suppress Bandits: Gangs of bandits are causing disturbances in Juegang, and the situation is critical. The district office in that area has telegraphed the county government for help. In addition to dispatching troops for reinforcements, the county government has also telegraphed the Haian Huangqiao Provincial Police Headquarters, requesting them to send troops to suppress the bandits.

Jiangyin 74

Prisoner Dies of Illness in Jail: Thirty prisoners were sent to Jiangyin by the High Court. Besides the executed Lu Caidi, Shi Zixin, a native of Nantong, who was sentenced to ten years for an appeal in the Haimen robbery case, died of pulmonary tuberculosis in prison on the 24th. The county conducted an autopsy to verify the cause of death and reported it to the court for record.

Thieves Sentenced to Imprisonment: Han Hongzhao and Wang Xiaofa from Dingshi were sentenced to three years and six months each by the county for robbing the Wang Hengshan home. Yin Hezhang, Wu Zihe from Yuqi in Wuxi, and Tao Apang were sentenced to six months each by the county for stealing from the Wu Hesheng home. Han and the others have appealed to the High Court against the original sentence. The county dispatched police escorts to Suzhou for a hearing on the 25th.

Taizhou 75

Large-Scale Joint Suppression of Bandits and Communists: In the western townships of Linhai, over a thousand bandits and communists have gathered in recent days. On Xiaori day, they attacked and confiscated the weapons from the 7th company of the 2nd battalion of the 5th regiment in this township's Huxian, Xiatang, and Yuanmao Liangdian, and are now approaching the county seat. The county government, the county party headquarters, and local organizations have repeatedly telegraphed the provincial government. The provincial government has specially dispatched Li's Brigade from Wenzhou and Zhu's Regiment from Taizhou to jointly suppress the bandits and communists. The forces have now been concentrated in the county seat and are scheduled to launch a multi-pronged attack on the 23rd.

Page 11

Local Correspondence Two

Zhenjiang 76

Merchants Request Postponement of House Demolition: The Jiangsu Provincial Capital Construction Committee previously planned to build a road from Xinximen Zhugang Xiang to Beimeng Mall. The route has been designated, and a notice has been issued to demolish houses on both sides of the road by the end of March to facilitate construction. The deadline is approaching, and residents in the Wangjinqiao to Xiaoshikou area have complied with the demolition. However, the area from Wutiaojie to Zhugangxiang is mostly shops, and the houses were rebuilt after the provincial government moved to Zhenjiang. The merchants jointly submitted a petition to the Jiangsu Provincial Capital Construction Committee and the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department, requesting an extension of the demolition period to allow them to close their businesses.

Sports Association Organizes a Visiting Group: The Jiangsu Provincial Public Sports Field Federation previously resolved to organize a National Games visiting group at a temporary representative meeting. The group is scheduled to gather at the Yiti Yu Field in Shanghai at 2:00 PM on March 30th to visit Hangzhou. As the deadline is approaching, the association has sent notices to each county, requesting them to nominate one representative to go to Shanghai on time to organize a visiting group to go to Hangzhou together.

Yangzhou 77

Summons for Book Seller Accused of Selling Books: Wu Shaozi's family in Beihexia in this city planned to sell the books collected by the owner of Ce Hai Lou for about 30,000 yuan.

Book dealer Wang Xizhi learned about this and accused them of cultural affairs, so he appealed to the Education Bureau of the Education Department and the county government, etc. The department has now ordered the county government to thoroughly investigate and report, and summoned the original defendants to court for questioning. After receiving the order, the county government issued a summons to the Wu family for questioning, and at the same time consulted the Yangzhou Customs to instruct the customs at various passes to detain the books if they were exported.

Qingjiang 78

Case of Injury and Death in Front of Yuantong Temple: In front of Yuantong Temple outside Dongyu in this port, which belongs to the jurisdiction of Huai'an County, Zhu Yuzhen's family, who are Fengshui masters, was suddenly attacked by more than 20 bandits with quick-firing guns and Mauser pistols at 7:00 PM on the 21st, before sunset, who broke into the door. Yuzhen's younger brother, Xizhen, was shot in the head and immediately fell to the ground and died. The bandit kidnapped his younger brother's wife, Yang, and his son's wife, Du. Yuzhen's wife, Ma, was shot in the arm by the bandits' guns, and his son, Jinzhi, was shot in the leg by the bandits' guns. On the 22nd at dawn, they all came to Renzi Hospital in this port for treatment.

Funing 79

Giant Fish Discovered at the Entrance of the Lake: The east side of this county faces the sea. It has been raining continuously for days. Last night, there was wind and rain, and thunder rumbled. When the rain stopped at dawn, a large dead fish was suddenly discovered at Laohu in the Sheyang Lake estuary. It was shaped like a horse, more than ten feet tall, and more than ten feet long, weighing more than 300 dan. The hungry fishermen and boatmen nearby were horrified and immediately divided the fish for meat to stave off hunger for several days, and the rest was sold to towns and cities, earning a considerable sum.

Appeal Against Locking Up the Chief of the Branch Bureau Dismissed: Guo Wenhua, the chief of the Banhu Town Public Security Branch Bureau in this county, was previously taken into custody by Guan Naiqing and others, who used weapons to confiscate the guns of the patrol officers of the bureau and locked up Chief Guo with iron chains, sending him to the county government. The county government immediately tried the case. The county government held that Guan Naiqing and others dared to bind and imprison personnel performing public duties, so Guan and others were taken into custody. Guan Nai did not accept this and appealed to the High Court of Branch, requesting a transfer of jurisdiction. The court now issued a ruling stating that the request was without reason and should be dismissed, and the original county should adjudicate according to the law.

Nanjing 80

Reorganization of the China Li Education General Association: The China Li Education Alcohol and Tobacco Prohibition General Association is a national leader in Li Education. The association's standing committee members, Zhang Wanyou, Zhou Qilu, Shi Qinglin, Luo Tianhang, and others, noting that the internal organization of the Li Education Association is rather complex, the work of drug resistance has been largely ineffective, and the names are inconsistent, decided to reorganize it based on old cases. They have submitted the proposal to the Executive Yuan for record and requested that a general order be issued to protect its affiliated branches. The President of the Executive Yuan, after receiving the proposal, ordered the Secretariat to send a letter to the Ministry of Interior for approval and response. Yesterday, the association received a notice from the Ministry of Interior.

Jiaxing 81

Butcher Industry Opposes Increasing Slaughter Surtax: At the Jiaxing County Council meeting, it was resolved to increase the slaughter surtax by 40% to allocate funds for public welfare education. The resolution will be implemented soon. The Butcher Industry Branch has argued that the slaughter surtax already includes donations for public welfare and education, and the additional 40% increase would be an unbearable burden. They have submitted a petition to the county government, requesting that the resolution not be implemented to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants, and they have sent a telegram to the provincial government, calling for help. It is unknown what the authorities will do about this.

Jiashan 82

Qinghe Merchant Ship Robbed: The Qinghe merchant ship, which sails between Jiashan and Luxu, was robbed on the 25th. When sailing from Shan to Luxu, about three li from Xitang near Fanqing, it was suddenly attacked by several bandit ships with more than a dozen bandits armed with wooden-cased guns and quick-firing guns. They robbed passengers of their clothing, jewelry, silver, and other items. In the ship, there was a partner from a certain village in the city carrying $5,000 in banknotes to Xitang, who was also robbed. At that time, the telephone line in Shanxi was interrupted. A fast messenger flew to report to the city's water and land agencies. The County Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched detectives to track them down, but no trace was found.

Huzhou 83

Fire in Taihefang: At 10:30 AM today, a fire broke out on the upper floor of the Yuantong Straw Hat Company in Taihefang in this city, causing a blaze. The fire brigades of each shop in the city rushed to the scene after receiving the alarm, but because it was inconvenient to get water at that location, it was difficult to put out the fire for a while, and it took an hour to extinguish it. Nine companies were burned: Yuantong Company, Gongxingchang Machine Material Store, Shengji Restaurant, Baoming Gasoline Lamp Company, Zhangyuansheng Silk Store, Xinchengtai Iron Factory, Juchang Silk Store, Yeheshang Congee Store, and Tanghongxing Congee Store, as well as more than ten houses.

Shen Haichi's Home Set on Fire by Bandits: Shen Haichi, a resident of Zhaocun in Chengjing Village, Huzhou, had his home robbed by bandits. Recently, he has repeatedly received threatening letters from bandits, which he ignored. On the night of the 22nd of this month, about 20 bandits suddenly came to the village, entered Shen's home armed, and set fire to three halls. When the villagers saw the bandits going away, they gathered to put out the fire, and the neighboring houses were not affected.

Education News: Sports

Championship Tournament: China Wins Championship 84

Yesterday with 52 to 27

Defeated the Sea Monster Pittsburgh Team

The Chinese Basketball Team and the Sea Monster Pittsburgh team agreed to a championship tournament to compete for maritime supremacy. In the first game, China won with 47 to 40. Last night, in the second game, China won again with 52 to 27, securing the championship tournament. The third game will still be held on Saturday night of this week, but the outcome is of no consequence to the championship. The referee was Mr. Beyliss and the inspector was Mr. Le Xiurong.

Referee Reduces Excitement

The referee occupies an important position in the battle, increasing the spirit of combat on both sides and adding to the enthusiasm of the audience. This depends on strict rules and decisive decision-making. Last night, the players of both teams, especially the Pittsburgh team, had many fouls, but the referee was not experienced enough, was slow to judge, and did not enforce the rules strictly, which reduced the color of the exciting and interesting ball battle.

Chinese Team is Outstanding

Yesterday's performance of the Chinese team can be described as outstanding, even more brilliant than last time, with internal and external consistency, and good offense and defense. The Pittsburgh team paled in comparison, could not catch up, and admitted defeat.

Pittsburgh Team Competes Vigorously

The Chinese team took the lead, first with a strong hand, initially taking the lead with eight to three. The Pittsburgh team changed its strategy, alternating inside and outside, and the situation quickly became a confrontation, neck and neck. Although China repeatedly took the lead and led, the Pittsburgh team followed closely, the distance between them was very small. In the first half, China was twenty-two and the Pittsburgh team was eighteen.

Chinese Team Works Harder

In the second half, the battle lines of both sides remained the same. The Pittsburgh team made a splash, adding two goals in a row, making the score 22 points apiece. The audience was alarmed. The Chinese team worked harder, bravely took the lead, and suddenly the spirit was full of energy, and the momentum was a hundredfold. From then on, it was smooth sailing, reaching the realm of success. After 26 to 23 (China took the lead), the Pittsburgh team retreated and never recovered, almost failing to be the sea monster.

National Women's Basketball Tournament: China Achieves First Victory 85

Yesterday's Score: 17-15 Victory Over Great Britain

USA Defeats Federation: 27-23

China Defeats Great Britain: Since the beginning of the Shanghai National Women's Basketball Championship, the Chinese team had been defeated in every match. However, at 7 PM last night, they unexpectedly defeated Great Britain by a margin of two points, with a score of 17-15. The performance of both sides was not particularly outstanding. On the Chinese team, the forwards Guo Xiaoping and Xi Jun were better players. Chen Xinyuan was slightly slow, while the defender Jiang Huaixuan showed great effort. Hua Fuji was also small but fought bravely. She Qiying had the disadvantage of focusing on the person instead of the ball. After the start of the game, Great Britain took the lead all the way, never falling behind. By the end of the first half, China suddenly took the lead with a score of 12-10. In the afternoon, Great Britain's momentum surged again, causing China to fall behind. In the last eight minutes, the Chinese women made continuous efforts and achieved remarkable results, finally defeating Great Britain with a score of 17-15.

First Quarter: China 4 points, Great Britain 8 points

Second Quarter: China 8 points, Great Britain 2 points

Third Quarter: China 0 points, Great Britain 5 points

Fourth Quarter: China 5 points, Great Britain 0 points

USA Defeats Federation: The USA and the Federation were the most promising teams in this championship. In the past, each side had lost once. Last night's second encounter was virtually a decisive battle. In the first half, the USA showed great strength, winning with a score of 16-10. In the second half, the Federation launched a fierce counterattack, but because they were too far behind in the first half, the USA still won with a score of 27-23. The scores for each quarter are as follows:

First Quarter: USA 7 points, Federation 5 points

Second Quarter: USA 9 points, Federation 5 points

Third Quarter: USA 8 points, Federation 4 points

Fourth Quarter: USA 3 points, Federation 9 points

The Shanghai Municipal Government, in order to inspire physical education and encourage progress, has specially prepared various awards to be sent to Hangzhou and has dispatched Councilor Tang Naikang to attend and observe.

The Preparatory Office of the National Games believes that during the opening of the games, more than 2,000 athletes from across the country will gather in Hangzhou. They have already contacted the Shanghai Qianghua Company and arranged to screen a film every other night, each time changing to a famous blockbuster. Grand Welcome of Athletes by the Commercial Press 98

Yesterday afternoon at around 4 PM, the Commercial Press of Shanghai hosted a banquet for athletes from the North and South at the China Basketball Hall, with over 200 people in attendance. During the banquet, the Commercial Press distributed various pamphlets and books as souvenirs. Huang Jingwan took the lead to stand up and speak, in a humorous and witty manner, saying, "It is a great honor to have so many athletes from the North and South here today. The colleagues of the Commercial Press sincerely welcome you. However, the refreshments are a bit simple and not very elegant." Subsequently, Wu Dongchu of the Commercial Press delivered a welcome speech, saying that failure is the mother of success, and China's sports cannot yet be compared with those of the great powers. However, seeing the vibrant spirit of everyone today is encouraging. Finally, Hao Boyang gave a speech, saying, "I just returned from overseas. What I can say about sports in foreign countries is (1) a spirit of benevolence permeates everything, not only rejoicing in the joy of others but also worrying about their worries. Whenever the other party is injured or encounters misfortune, there is a strong sense of sympathy and tenderness; (2) not taking victory as the goal, but engaging in the study of technology. After each game, the losers carefully consider the reasons for their own failure and the reasons for the other party's victory, diligently seeking to deepen their skills. The above two points are indeed good habits on foreign sports fields and also good examples for Chinese athletes. In recent years, interest in sports in our country has increased dramatically. Take football as an example. In the past, there were only five or six hundred spectators, but now there are more than ten thousand. The difference is like heaven and earth. I sincerely hope that everyone will pay more attention to the 'spirit of chivalry' in sports during this sports boom, and I wish you all smooth sailing, hoping to win championships in this National Games and strive for a place in the future Far Eastern Games, so that one day there will be Chinese athletes in the World Games." After the photo session, the guests and hosts parted happily, and the clock had already struck past 5 PM.

Important News

Ministry of Education Emphasizes Education for Mongol and Tibetan People 102

In order to actively promote education for Mongol and Tibetan people, the Ministry of Education has issued a special order to implement Mongol and Tibetan education in various leagues and banners in the provinces. It is noted that popular education is a fundamental plan for popularizing education. The Mongol and Tibetan regions are located in remote border areas, and popular education is extremely rudimentary. In order to implement popularization and develop border education, the establishment of schools for the people is an urgent matter. However, the establishment of public schools must first focus on teaching materials. The situation in Mongolia and Tibet is special, and the teaching materials adopted should be based on local conditions and the people's lives and customs as the standard. The Ministry is now planning to compile popular reading materials and urgently needs to collect various popular reading materials related to folk customs and habits, such as songs and legends, for reference. In addition to separate orders, an order is hereby given to the banner to quickly collect all kinds of popular reading materials from the people, both in Chinese and Mongolian, for submission to the ministry for review. This is extremely important. This order.

Ministry of Education Orders Qun Zhi Summer School to Close 103

The Ministry of Education previously received a declaration of withdrawal from students of the Shanghai Private Qun Zhi University, listing the school's mismanagement. The Shanghai Special City Education Bureau was immediately ordered to investigate the facts. The bureau has now submitted a reply, stating that the school has only seven classrooms, simple equipment, incomplete books, financial difficulties, corrupt content, and frequent disputes. It is heard that the Ministry of Education has instructed the City Education Bureau to order the school to close during the summer vacation of this year.

Request from the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Association 104

The Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Association has recently submitted six documents to the Education Department and the Jiangsu Education Funding Committee: (1) requesting that education bureaus in various counties be instructed to give priority to graduates of normal schools and normal school students for primary school teachers. Those who drop out of normal school should be responsible for recovering various fees or compensating for them; (2) requesting the prompt allocation of temporary fees for the eighteenth year in order to repay advances or carry out construction and equipment projects; (3) requesting that the top two students with the best academic performance in each senior high school graduating class be recommended to the Central University for admission without examination to encourage them; (4) requesting that the Jiangsu Education Funding Committee increase the living expenses for normal school students; (5) requesting that because the calculation forms for each month of the first semester of the eighteenth year have been completed and cannot be changed, permission be granted to instruct all schools to report using the new calculation forms from January of the nineteenth year; (6) requesting clarification on whether the expenses for student visits and educational trips should be subsidized by the school and how to raise the funds, so that they can be complied with.

The Grand Welcome to the Athlete by the Commercial Press 108

Around 4 p.m. yesterday afternoon, the Commercial Press hosted a banquet at the Chinese Basketball Stadium for athletes from the North and South, with over 200 people in attendance. The Commercial Press also distributed small books and other materials to commemorate the event. Huang Jingwan first stood up to speak in a grave, yet comic, tone and said: "We are honored to have so many athletes from the North and South here today. On behalf of all of my colleagues here at the Commercial Press, I'd like to extend a heartfelt welcome. However, the refreshments are meager." Following this, Wu Dongchu from the Commercial Press gave a welcome speech, saying that failure is the mother of success. China's sporting achievements are still not yet able to compete with the world powers; however, seeing these athletes here today is very promising. Finally, Hao Boyang delivered a speech saying, "I have recently returned from overseas, and there are a few things to be said about sports in other countries. The first is that they are able to maintain a spirit of benevolence, not only rejoicing in the successes of others, but also worrying about their failures. Whenever opponents are injured or suffer, they are treated with great compassion. Second, their aim is not only victory but study, each time considering why they have lost, or why their opponents have won, and striving to improve. These two principles are the characteristics of sportsmen in foreign countries and should be emulated by our sportsmen. As for our nation, interest in sports has grown rapidly in recent years. As for football, for example, in the past there were only five or six hundred spectators, but now there are more than ten thousand. It is hoped that everyone present will pay attention to the spirit of justice and altruism in the current sports boom. I would also like to wish that you will achieve victory during the National Games and win awards at the Far Eastern Games so that our Chinese sportsmen may one day compete in the World Games". A commemorative photo was then taken.

City Education Bureau Convenes Kindergarten Teaching Discussion 111

On March 22nd, the City Education Bureau convened the first meeting of the Kindergarten Teaching Discussion. Attendees included Xu Yamin, Lu Ping, Gu Bao Fan, Zhang Lizhen, Zhang Jianhua, Shen Muzhen, Yang Zhiru, Zhang Li, Wu Peixuan, Guo Wennong, Zhang Qinlan, Song Jianqing, Li Baozhen, Wang Jiying, and Tu Zhemei. The chair was Tu Zhemei, and the recorder was Yang Zhiru. The meeting commenced with customary formalities.

1. Chairman's Report.

2. Resolutions:

1. The meeting date is set for the fourth Friday of each month, from 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM.

2. The next meeting location is set at the Jiangwan Xijiang Girls' School Kindergarten. If there are any changes, the instructor will be notified first, and then a letter will be sent to notify each kindergarten.

3. The meeting locations will be rotated among the kindergartens. If the weather is good, the meeting can be held outdoors or in a park.

4. During the meeting, each kindergarten should contribute teaching materials as much as possible for exchange.

5. Please have the instructor collect more singing teaching materials and introduce applicable educational toys and teaching aids for reference.

6. Meeting notices will be issued by the Bureau to the principals of each school to be passed on to the kindergarten teachers. Those who are independently organized will be directly notified.

7. Meeting reception fees will be handled by the rotating kindergartens themselves.

8. The rotating kindergartens should especially exhibit children's various achievements, toys, teaching aids, teaching materials for each subject, various forms, curriculum diaries, and other research or records during the meeting.

9. If any kindergarten has difficult questions, please submit the questions to the Bureau at any time for answers.

City Education Bureau Orders Private Universities to Organize Advancement and Employment Guidance Sub-Committees 113

The Shanghai Special City Education Bureau yesterday ordered all private universities to comply. For the purpose of guiding students of all levels of schools in advancement to higher education and employment, the Bureau has organized an Advancement and Employment Guidance Committee and formulated committee regulations, which have been separately issued to municipal schools of all levels for compliance and implementation. For this reason, a copy of the regulations is issued, instructing your university to quickly comply and organize a sub-committee, carefully formulate methods, earnestly implement guidance, and report the organizational situation and the name of the chairperson for record. This order is attached with the Advancement and Employment Guidance Committee Regulations.

Article 1: Matters concerning the guidance of students of all levels of schools in this city and students from other places in Shanghai for advancement to higher education or employment shall be handled by this Committee under the direction of the Bureau Director.

Article 2: This Committee shall be organized by the Bureau with the appointment of a certain number of people.

Article 3: This Committee shall have a chairperson and a secretary, each appointed by the Bureau Director from among the members.

Article 4: This Committee may designate schools of all levels to organize Advancement and Employment Guidance Committee sub-committees. The sub-committee members mentioned in the previous article shall be filled by the principals, deans of academic affairs, deans of student affairs, main teachers, and a number of experts from each school. The principal or dean of academic affairs shall serve as the chairperson.

Article 5: Each sub-committee must report the progress and results of implementing advancement and employment guidance to this Committee.

Article 6: Students from other places in Shanghai seeking advancement to higher education or employment may come to this Committee to request guidance.

Article 7: This Committee shall hold a regular meeting once a month. When necessary, special meetings may be held, all of which shall be convened by the chairperson.

Article 8: These regulations shall be implemented after being approved by the Bureau Affairs Meeting.

Biology Institute PhD Zhu Henian Returns to China 115

Dr. Zhu Henian is the third son of the famous Shanghai doctor Zhu Nanshan. In 1926, he graduated from Fudan University with a degree in psychology and continued his research at the university for one year. In August 1927, he went to the United States to study biological sciences at the University of Chicago. In February of this year, he obtained a PhD degree. His thesis has won praise from people in that country. It is reported that he has now arrived in Kobe, Japan, and plans to stay for one or two months before taking the American ship Jefferson to return to China on the 25th.

Local News

Government and Business Rescue the Rice Shortage 116

Price limited to 20 yuan

Subsidized sales to be held

Checking stock in production areas

Reasons for Rice Price Increase: The price of rice has been soaring for days, even exceeding 20 yuan. According to investigations, in addition to the scarcity of goods arriving from various places, the main reason is that the output of foreign rice from Saigon and other places has recently decreased, and procurement has become difficult. As a result, the original price has risen sharply. The recent import cost is estimated at 20 yuan and 5 jiao per 200 pounds, an increase of nearly 10% in the past two weeks. As a result, the price of rice has continued to rise. In recent days, rice merchants from various places have ordered approximately 500,000 tons of new rice from Saigon and other places for May delivery, and approximately 300,000 tons for June delivery. The price is around 20 yuan, so the price of rice is unlikely to fall in the short term.

Government Price Limit: The Municipal Social Bureau, in response to the continuous rise in rice prices in this city, has received reports from the Food Committee and has long been preparing for subsidized rice sales, but has not yet been able to hold them due to the difficulty in raising large sums of money. However, a Rice Subsidized Price Committee has been established and is purchasing 200,000 bags of foreign rice to handle subsidized sales, which has been submitted to the mayor for approval. Yesterday, the price of special japonica rice in the northern city was as high as 21 yuan and 2 jiao per stone, so a public notice has been issued (see today's newspaper advertisement) temporarily limiting the highest price of white rice to 20 yuan per stone, with lower grades priced separately. In the meantime, other methods are being considered to stabilize rice prices and prioritize people's livelihoods.

Rice Merchant Meeting: Ye Huijun, chairman of the Bean and Rice Industry Association, believes that the current time is spring, and it is not yet the time of year when supplies are scarce, but top-quality rice has already risen to more than 20 yuan, and medium-quality rice also requires 18 or 19 yuan. If relief is not planned in advance, the consequences would be unthinkable. Yesterday, he specially discussed with the leaders of the rice industry. Ye said, "The recent rise in rice prices is really due to the poor harvest in the production areas last year, which has led to a weak supply. Fortunately, foreign rice is being shipped to Shanghai for relief, otherwise it would be even worse. However, the rice-producing areas such as Saigon have seen a surge in procurement by Shanghai merchants, and prices have also risen. This year's foreign rice has risen by one yuan and several jiao compared to last year, which is an especially unusual situation." After discussion, the Rice Industry Federation was asked to send letters to various production areas to investigate the stock in the production areas for reference, so as to have a grasp of the situation. At the same time, fellow traders were informed that in case of shortage, buyers should be advised not to rush or over-collect, and customers should be instructed to put samples on sale as soon as the goods arrive, so as to prevent the market from being short of goods and alleviate the current market situation.

Report of Financial Advisor 117

Ministry of Finance to Announce on Sunday

In order to reform China's finances, the Ministry of Finance previously hired the Kemmerer Commission, a group of American financial experts, to serve as advisors. The Kemmerer Commission came to China last year in response to the invitation, studied various financial issues in China, and prepared a voluminous report containing recommendations. Since the report was submitted to Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance, it has not yet been released, so its contents are unknown to the outside world. It is now learned that the Ministry of Finance has decided to officially publish the report to give all sectors the opportunity to study it at length. As for the date of publication, it is said to have been decided as Sunday.

Notice of Inspection of Exported Raw Silk 123

Starting April 1st

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, under orders, scheduled the inspection of exported Chinese silk. Subsequently, because the manufacturers were not prepared in time, they continued to apply for an extension until April 1st. Because the deadline is approaching, all Chinese silk merchants were specifically notified yesterday that from April 1st, all exported raw silk must be sent to the Raw Silk Inspection Office for public measurement and inspection and to obtain inspection certificates in order to be verified and released by the Customs. The silk spun from Shuang Gong cocoons, silk head scraps, long and short silk filaments, and sample silks that do not fill a bag are all exempt from inspection. All silk merchants were notified to check accordingly yesterday.

Letter Requesting Delay of Overseas Chinese Postal Fees Increase 124

The Overseas Chinese Federation of the Republic of China yesterday sent a letter to the Postal Administration of the Ministry of Communications, which stated: "We are replying to your Bureau's letter No. 669 of March 26 of this year regarding the crackdown on general sealed packages from overseas Chinese private postal agencies. We have telegraphed the Kuala Lumpur Post Office and received a reply stating that the office did not declare to the overseas Chinese representatives that the case was initiated by the Chinese government. Now the government of the Malay Archipelago has notified that the increase in postal fees will be implemented from April 1st of this year. A corresponding letter is sent requesting support and guidance." On the same day, a letter from Lin Jindian, Chairman of the Xinjiapo (Singapore) Petition for Postal Fee Reduction, stated: "The Resident Overseas Chinese Representative Assembly has petitioned the residential government to extend the implementation for four months in order to resolve the petition and revoke the decision." This has been received.

"The Singapore government's reply to the overseas Chinese representatives was based on inquiries to the Kuala Lumpur Post Office, which is irrelevant and cannot be explained. Our association has again telegraphed the National Government requesting revocation. As instructed in the previous letter, we hereby reply to your Bureau for reference. Please immediately telegraph the Shantou and Xiamen post offices to postpone the implementation for four months in order to petition the government at home and abroad for a resolution. We hope you will act accordingly to promote public welfare. Respectfully, to the Postal Administration of the Ministry of Communications."

Committee for the Reorganization of Business Organizations Cables to Request Relief for Chinese Tobacco Merchants 126

The Committee for the Reorganization of Business Organizations cabled the Ministry of Finance yesterday to request relief for Chinese tobacco merchants, stating: "To the esteemed Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the 25th of this month, we received a respectful telegram from the Guangzhou Chinese Tobacco Commercial Association, stating that the selling price of cigarettes is based on the customs tax rate. Now it is being recalculated based on the gold price, and the tax amount has increased. Since the tax amount has increased, the original wholesale price should also increase accordingly. For other items, pricing is free, and although the tax amount has increased, it can be passed on. However, there are precedents for cigarette pricing that do not allow for arbitrary increases. If the tax amount increases but the wholesale price does not increase, the tax law is already unfair, and the losses are even more difficult to bear. We urgently telegram and appeal for permission to increase the wholesale price of cigarettes set by the Unified Tax Office based on the customs tax rate, in order to maintain the business. We hope that you will forward this request to the Ministry of Finance and the Cigarette Unified Tax Office. We would be immensely grateful. The association has repeatedly submitted detailed reports on the various painful situations of Chinese tobacco merchants, where the predetermined number of grades is too large and prices cannot be increased freely, and even though material costs have soared, they can only be sold at a loss, in various industrial plans for relief presented by the affiliated association, and in the previous two telegrams transferred from the association requesting relaxed price limits. The fundamental solution for relief is to change the unified tax to a two-tier collection system, as proposed in the document submitted by the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company to your department, which is the most thorough solution. Unfortunately, it has not been adopted, so that the suffering of tobacco merchants has not been alleviated, and the two factories of Nanyang Changxing in this city have also closed down due to deep losses. It is a tragedy that business is so difficult. Now that the Customs is levying taxes on cigarettes and their required materials based on the gold price, while the wholesale price is still fixed according to the old limits, it is impossible for tobacco merchants to continue to support the situation of selling at a loss with pain. The request to allow the Cigarette Unified Tax Office to increase the wholesale price of cigarettes based on the customs tax rate is a request that is urgently needed at the moment and is different from revising the unified tax grades, which require detailed review. As for your department's March 15th approval of the eastern telegraph of the affiliated association, it is stated that the sharp rise in gold prices not only affects the cigarette industry, and the government should plan for comprehensive relief, and that piecemeal relief is not allowed. It is understood that although various industries have been affected by the sharp rise in gold prices, they are still able to increase prices freely to compensate, which is completely different from the situation of the cigarette industry, which can only watch the gold price rise day by day and only sell at a loss. Moreover, it is difficult to make a decision on government relief to various industries, such as silk and shipping, which require the allocation of subsidies, as they involve public funds. As for relaxing the price limits, the issuance of an order from your department in the morning would immediately relieve the tobacco merchants' predicament in the evening, which would be a beneficial act at no cost. If it is necessary to wait for comprehensive planning and handle the matter together, we are sincerely afraid that it will take a long time, and all Chinese tobacco factories will inevitably close down before then. The repetition of Nanyang Changxing's previous situation is unbearable. Therefore, we have quickly expressed our concerns and submitted this report with trepidation. We humbly request your department to promptly approve this request to relieve the imminent danger. We are overwhelmed with hope. Respectfully, the Shanghai Special City Merchant Groups Reorganization Committee."

County Readjustment Committee Meeting Minutes 128

Third Session

The Shanghai County Party Affairs Readjustment Committee held its third committee meeting yesterday. Attendees included Jiang Wenbao, Liu Rentao, Lü Zhe, and Wu Jingqing. Jiang Wenbao chaired the meeting, with Chen Jiapu as the recorder. After standard formalities, the meeting commenced with a brief report on matters. Then, the discussion of proposals began: (1) Proposal regarding subsidies for lower-level party branches: It was resolved (1) to submit a request to the Provincial Party Headquarters to instruct the Civil Affairs Department to allocate funds to the county, and (2) to raise the matter for discussion at the Party-Government Talks. (2) Proposal regarding the commencement of work by the committee, which should involve thoroughly inspecting the recent situation of lower-level party branches in each district and the ideological and behavioral state of party members throughout the county to determine a readjustment plan: Resolved, passed. Wu Jingqing and Liu Rentao were nominated to draft regulations and design forms. (3) Proposal regarding the inactive state of the County Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce Readjustment Committee and how to handle it: Resolved, to cease activities and hand over the task to the Training Department to draft a readjustment plan. (4) Proposal regarding how the committee should commemorate the 72 Martyrs' Memorial Day: Resolved, (1) the Propaganda Department should issue a notice to all levels of party branches to follow the Central Committee's prescribed commemorative methods; (2) a commemorative rally should be convened for all county-level agencies at 9:00 AM on that day. (5) Proposal to establish a small-scale reading room and club: Resolved, to be handled at the discretion of the Secretariat. (6) Proposal regarding a letter from the County Government requesting attendance at a defense conference: Resolved, to nominate Lü Zhe, Liu Rentao, and Wu Jingqing to attend. (7) Proposal regarding officials already appointed to the committee who have not yet reported for duty: Resolved, (1) to send letters through their introducers, urging them to report within a week; (2) living expenses should be paid from the date of their arrival. (8) Proposal to schedule a Party-Government Talks session for 2:00 PM on April 2nd: Resolved, passed.

Baoshan County Party Headquarters: Zhang Yahua and Others Released on Bail by Provincial Order 129

Zhang Yahua, Zhu Shengmo, and Wang Yibing, former executive committee members of the Baoshan County Party Headquarters, were arrested on December 17th of last year on suspicion of being reactionary elements, as per a telegram order from Miao Bin, the director of the Civil Affairs Department of Jiangsu Province. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. Subsequently, various sectors of Baoshan made multiple efforts to rescue them, but to no avail. Zhu Shengmo was released on bail due to illness. Zhang and Wang have been detained for over three months. The Baoshan County Magistrate, Wu Jianong, received instructions from the Civil Affairs Department on the 25th (day before yesterday), stating that Zhang Yahua and others had been investigated by the Readjustment Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters and found to have no reactionary behavior. He was ordered to instruct the County Public Security Bureau to release them on bail. Upon receiving the order, Magistrate Wu immediately instructed Shen Qing, the director of the County Public Security Bureau, to find guarantors for Zhang Yahua and others, and they were released at 6:00 PM the day before yesterday.

General Manager of the Gas Company Denies Making Statements 130

Conversations Published in the Wenhui Bao

On the 20th of this month, the Wenhui Bao reported that Canning, the General Manager of the Shanghai Gas Company, had made a four-point statement to the newspaper representative regarding the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau's deadline for signing a contract with the Municipal Government: (1) The company supplies gas to 30 foreign households in Zhabei, and the Chinese authorities are demanding a share of the profits; (2) Until last year, the company paid 1,000 taels of silver annually for road excavation fees, but stopped paying in April of last year due to continuous demands from the Public Utilities Bureau; (3) The company treats the authorities in both the Chinese and foreign concessions equally; (4) It is not justified for Chinese to demand a share of the profits based on the fact that foreigners outside the concession are using the company's gas. Upon seeing this news, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau listed the facts and refuted each point of the aforementioned person's statement, disclosing them in various Chinese and foreign newspapers in the city on the 22nd. On the same day, it also sent a serious letter of inquiry to the said person. It was learned yesterday that the said person had officially replied to Director Huang of the Bureau, stating that he had not made the aforementioned statement to the Wenhui Bao representative. He also made some statements regarding the reasons for the delay in signing the contract. The original letter is translated and published below: In response to your letter of the 22nd of this month, I declare that I did not have a conversation with a Wenhui Bao representative. It was not until I read the Dalu News on the 24th that I learned about the matter. However, on the morning of the 20th, indeed, a reporter from that newspaper came to the office, holding a clipping from The Times newspaper, asking about the gas company receiving a final notice from the Public Utilities Bureau. I replied that I knew nothing about the matter and had nothing to say. After the reporter left, Mr. Potter (i.e., the company's Chief Engineer) arrived, carrying your Bureau's letter of the 19th (i.e., the letter giving a final consideration deadline). When asked what it was about, we discussed your letter in detail, believing that a face-to-face meeting would be the most appropriate. Therefore, Mr. Potter sent a letter to arrange a meeting. As for your belief that the delay in signing the contract is due to the fact that the contract must be translated into English before formally seeking opinions from all parties, it is because the directors of a limited company must be responsible to the shareholders. It can be asserted that the gas company is willing to contribute to society in order to enjoy the franchise. We believe that after our explanation, your office will understand the company's position. It was also learned that yesterday (the 26th) at 10:30 AM, Canning, the General Manager of the company, and Potter, the Chief Engineer, went to the Bureau as scheduled to discuss the contract signing issue. It is reported that the company agreed to all the conditions in the contract and expressed its willingness to sign at any time. However, regarding Article 8, which requires the Municipal Government to order the relocation of gas pipes within a specified period, and Article 11, which requires the annual settlement and payment of additional guarantee money due to the increase in pipelines, they requested slight changes. The Bureau agreed to forward the request to the Bureau of Industry and Commerce for consideration and promised to respond to the company within a few days before scheduling the contract signing again.

Oil Depots in the City Must Be Moved to Laoshu Sha 131

Notices from the Bureau of Public Works and the Land Bureau to Various Oil Companies to Comply. The Bureau of Public Works and the Land Bureau, following instructions from the Municipal Government, in accordance with a letter from the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee, based on the resolution of the Fourth Representative Assembly of the Fifth District Party Headquarters, requesting the Municipal Government to ban oil depots near the Gao Miao area of the Lühang District, etc., designated Laoshu Sha as the oil depot area of the city. This was intended to ban oil depots in Pudong and Puxi to avoid danger. The oil depots in the Shangmiao area of the Lühang District are naturally included in the ban. The Bureau of Public Works and the Land Bureau were instructed to jointly notify all oil merchants to immediately move all oil depots to Laoshu Sha to ensure safety, etc. It is reported that the Bureau of Public Works and the Land Bureau have followed the order and jointly notified Mobil, Asiatic Petroleum, Texaco, Guangyu, and other oil companies that if they need to build additional oil depots in the future, they should comply with the eight measures for delineating the oil depot area. All oil depots already built outside the oil depot area should also be moved to the oil depot area as soon as possible to ensure safety.

Shipping News 132

Fog Obstruction of Ships Entering Port. Heavy fog occurred outside Wusong the night before last, obstructing nearly twenty Chinese and foreign merchant ships from entering the port. By yesterday morning, the fog had dissipated, and the ships began to arrive in Shanghai one after another. However, the American Mail Line's President Jefferson ran aground on the 25th due to low tide and was unable to move, obstructing many ships coming to Shanghai behind it. It was not until 11:30 AM yesterday that the Jefferson was able to take advantage of the rising tide, leave the shallows, and enter the Huangpu River. The merchant ships that were backed up behind it were also able to gradually enter Wusong. By 4:00 PM, as many as thirty-two merchant ships had arrived in Shanghai. The Jianghe and other ships, due to the delay in entering the port, are planning to postpone their departure by one day.

Unloading and Inspection of Damaged Ship Cargo. The Nippon Yusen Kaisha's Kasato Maru was damaged in Kobe harbor by the Osaka Shosen Kaisha's American merchant ship Arabia Maru, and much of the cargo in the hold was stained and damaged by water. The cargo has now been loaded onto the Mikasa Maru and brought to Shanghai. Yesterday, the company notified all consignees that the stained and damaged cargo from the Kasato Maru will be handled in accordance with the law of general average. It has been decided that the cargo will be unloaded and inspected at the Yangshupu Huishan Wharf this morning, with the inspection conducted by a surveyor. Consignees are requested to send representatives to the site for joint inspection. In addition, the damaged cargo on the Nisshin Kisen's Ba Ling Maru is also being unloaded in Pudong, and a date will be set for a joint inspection of the damage. Furthermore, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Ming entered port this time with 444 bags of flour and over 70 pieces of miscellaneous goods in the second hold that were damaged by seawater. The company has ordered the business department to thoroughly investigate the cause of the damage.

Sharp Reduction in Chinese Ships to Fuzhou. There were originally four Chinese ships operating on the Shanghai-Fuzhou route. After suspending service last winter, service only resumed in the middle of this month. However, most of the cargo on that route has been taken by Japanese ships. By the time the Chinese ships resumed operations, there was no cargo to load. Therefore, the Ningshao Company first stopped the Yongxing on the Shanghai-Min route and reassigned it to the Yangtze River route. Yesterday, the Sanbei Company also reassigned the Xin Ningxing to the Yangtze River route, leaving only two ships operating on the Fuzhou route.

Japanese Merchants Increase Ships in North China. Kawasaki Kisen Kaisha, a Japanese company, originally used six ships this year to operate three coastal routes in China. Now, they have added a newly built 3,500-ton ship, the Kei Saki Maru, to Shanghai. It has already arrived in Shanghai. It was originally intended to operate on the Zhejiang-Min coastal route, but due to the relatively large number of passengers traveling to and from North China, it has been approved to start its maiden voyage from Shanghai to Tianjin today.

Sino-European Shipping News 133

Italian Mail Ships Cease Passenger Service. Since the Italian Mail Line in Shanghai added four new motor engine oil-powered mail ships last year, it has been paying great attention to carrying passengers. Each month, a formal mail ship is operated, with cabins divided into first class and third class. After last autumn, four cargo-only ships were added to the Sino-Italian route, running once every six months, without passengers. There has been a significant improvement in the transport of Italian goods recently, with sesame and ramie being the largest export to that country. Each ship now carries over 10,000 bags. Recently, the Shanghai branch received a telegram from the Italian headquarters stating that passenger service on ships from Shanghai to Italy will be discontinued from June 4th. The Shanghai branch was ordered to end ticket sales by the end of May. Yesterday, the branch notified its branches in Tianjin, Hankou, and Lianyungang, instructing them to stop selling tickets for ships to Italy in June. The reason is unknown.

Changes in Transporting Goods to the Philippines. Shipments from Shanghai to North Africa were previously transported on European ships to Marseilles, France, and then transferred. Shipping costs were collected and guaranteed by shipping companies in Shanghai. The European Shipping Association in Shanghai specially invited representatives from various shipping companies and decided that from today, shipping companies will no longer guarantee the transport of goods from Shanghai to North Africa. They will only be carried to Marseilles, and those that need to be transferred to the Philippines will be transferred to North African ships in France. The freight will be paid by the cargo owners. The shipping rates agreed upon by the Shanghai Association are as follows: (1) To Tripoli, 16 shillings per ton of miscellaneous goods; (2) To Benghazi, 25 shillings per ton; (3) To Casablanca, Spain, 15 shillings per ton; (4) To Port Lyautey or Arzew, France, 20 shillings per ton; (5) To Safi, Rabat, and Bône in North Africa, 25 shillings per ton each. Yesterday, this measure was notified to twenty-five European shipping companies for consistent implementation.

Urging the Surrender of Embezzled Housing Tax by Former County Magistrates 134

Shao Shuhua and Jiang Jiazhui, former county magistrates of Shanghai County, embezzled housing tax funds during their terms of office. Although they have been out of office for some time, they have not yet surrendered the funds. Now, the County Local Assets Management Committee believes that the housing tax funds belong to the local area. If the funds are not urgently recovered, the matter will inevitably be delayed indefinitely. It was resolved at a recent meeting to specially urge the surrender of the funds. A letter was immediately sent to the County Government, and County Magistrate Leng instructed the Finance Bureau to comply yesterday.

The French-owned Pathé gramophone record factory on Xujiahui Road has been on strike for over ten days. Paris Maru Encountered Danger and Returned to Shanghai 139

The Nisshin Kisen Kaisha's Paris Maru ran aground near Shantou on the 28th of last month and was attacked by pirates, nearly sinking. Losses were significant. Fortunately, it was rescued by the Japanese Navy warship Kaki and inspected by Takeashita, the company's supervisor, who rushed to the scene. It was briefly repaired in Fuzhou and returned to Shanghai yesterday (the 26th) to enter the dock for repairs. Supervisor Takeashita has also returned to Shanghai.

The Enthusiasm of the Overseas Anti-Drug Movement 140

The Singapore Chin Woo Athletic Association Revived

The China National Anti-Narcotics Association has been making unremitting efforts to investigate and promote the anti-drug situation among overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia and the overseas anti-drug movement. Huang Jiawei, the general manager of the association, recently went to the British and Dutch territories in Southeast Asia for inspection and promotion, achieving great results. Wherever Mr. Huang went, he received enthusiastic responses, and the anti-drug voices suddenly became intense. Anti-drug organizations and smoking cessation hospitals are being actively organized in Singapore, Yogyakarta, Semarang, Batavia, Surabaya, Bandung, Medan, and other places. Local celebrities and enthusiastic overseas individuals are also actively participating. The Singapore Chin Woo Athletic Association was established 30 years ago and had branches throughout British territories such as Ipoh, Kuala Lumpur, Penang, and Malacca. It had branches in all these places. However, it was interrupted due to some events and has been suspended for 20 years. This time, thanks to Mr. Huang's advocacy and promotion, the people's spirit was greatly encouraged, leading to the revival of the Chin Woo Athletic Association. Other places are also actively preparing to cooperate with the China National Anti-Narcotics Association. The association received a telegram from the Singapore Chin Woo Athletic Association yesterday, reporting on the progress of the society after its establishment and the future direction of its work. More than ten important organizations and over one hundred and twenty individuals have joined.
