The Da Lun Real Estate Lawsuit: Appeal to the Supreme Court 143

Citing the Yan Mao Yuan Old Case

Demanding the Exercise of Ownership

Original Judgment from the Court of Appeal

A Concern for All Shanghai Citizens

Following the second instance judgment in the lawsuit between Da Lun Real Estate Company and its tenants, including Lao Da Fang, regarding relocation, the tenants were victorious. However, this case has drawn increased attention from those who own property. It is reported that Da Lun Company has received the judgment from the Court of Appeal.

The company has decided to file a third appeal with the Supreme Court in the capital, intending to cite the judgment in the case of Yan Mao Yuan Hotel versus landlord Ma Huanwen regarding relocation as the sole basis for the appeal. The Yan Mao Yuan's lawsuit against landlord Ma Huanwen for forced relocation was decided by the Provisional Court in July, ordering Yan Mao Yuan to relocate by July 15th. The judgment stated that the defendant's reconstruction of the house was based on the exercise of ownership, which is a disposition of property rights, and that the plaintiff, as a tenant, could not directly prevent the exercise of property rights based on the relationship of debt. Yan Mao Yuan, dissatisfied, appealed, but the Court of Appeal rejected the appeal and upheld the original judgment. The Court of Appeal's judgment also stated, "According to a lease agreement with no fixed term, the parties may request termination at any time." Da Lun argues that since the shops on Nanjing Road, Zhifu Li, leased by Lao Da Fang and others, do not have a lease specifying a term, the landlord's repossession for reconstruction is, in fact, an exercise of ownership and a disposition of property rights. They will now detail the reasons based on this interpretation, requesting a reversal from the Supreme Court. Therefore, the ultimate victor in this case remains to be seen. However, the Court of Appeal's judgment is also of great concern to all Shanghai citizens. We now present the full text of the judgment:

Appellants: Lao Da Fang Tea and Food Store and fifteen other households

Appellee: Da Lun Real Estate Company

Regarding the case of a lawsuit over the relocation of houses involving the aforementioned two parties, the appellants, dissatisfied with the first instance judgment made by the Shanghai Concession Provisional Court on November 21st of the 18th year of the Republic of China, appealed. This court's judgment is as follows:

(Main Text) The original judgment is reversed, except for the portions concerning Shi Wantai and Shao Wansheng. The appellee's lawsuit in the first instance is dismissed, except for the aforementioned portions. The costs of the first and second lawsuits shall be borne by the appellee. Lao Quan Chang's appeal shall be rejected, and the costs of the appeal shall be borne by Lao Quan Chang.

(Facts) The appellee owns houses located at the corner of Nanjing Road and Fujian Road and within Zhifu Li, which have been rented by the appellants. In October of the 17th year, the appellee leased the real estate to Da Zhonghua Department Store for reconstruction and business, and requested the appellants to vacate, but they were unwilling to relocate. The appellee sued, and the original trial ruled that the lease agreement should be terminated at the end of October of the 18th year, and that the defendants should return the houses within one month and twenty days after the termination. Based on the plaintiff's request, they were ordered to provide a security deposit of 20,000 taels of silver, which would be executed immediately. The appellants, dissatisfied, appealed. After the hearing began, the appellee withdrew the request for immediate execution and attempted mediation, which was unsuccessful. This is the factual background of the case. The appellants' statement requests the reversal of the original judgment and the dismissal of the appellee's lawsuit in the original trial. The main points of their appeal are as follows: Chinese merchants value good faith and trustworthiness above all else. Consensual contracts exist at any time. The appellants, Lao Da Fang, Yi An Ju, etc., certainly had an oral agreement with the deceased manager of the appellee, Sun Rongqing, at the beginning of the lease, specifying a lease term of 20 years. Pan Yuting, the brother of the manager Pan Jiaping, who was originally assigned the house in Yi An Ju, has already testified to this effect in the original trial and can be believed. Furthermore, the appellants who are renting the houses for business are also determined not to move frequently. The case of Yi An Ju is the same. By analogy, this can serve as proof that all other families must have had the same oral agreement. However, the original trial did not adopt this, which is difficult to accept. Moreover, according to Shanghai custom, unless (1) the landlord reclaims the house for their own use, (2) the tenant is three months in arrears of rent, or (3) the house is damaged and needs to be rebuilt, the landlord cannot order the tenant to relocate. Moreover, after reconstruction, the old tenant has a preferential right to lease. The Chinese Ratepayers' Association has issued a letter proving that this is the case. Now that the appellants are not in arrears of rent, and the houses were built less than ten years ago, and there is no need for reconstruction, the appellee is heeding Da Zhonghua Department Store's offer of higher rent and is not reclaiming it for its own use. Not only does this render the small rent spent by the appellants in the past and the huge amount of decoration that came with the house a waste of money, but it is also difficult to find a house to relocate to in the crowded city of Nanjing Road. It only seeks its own interests and disregards the interests of others. How can this be good for the social economy? What about the reputation of the business community? It is obviously contrary to general custom, and the law cannot recognize it. If it is said that the house ticket once stipulated that both parties could terminate the contract at any time, this one-sided, boilerplate document is clearly contrary to custom. How can it have a binding effect? The appellee's statement requests the rejection of the appeal and, ex officio, the declaration of immediate execution of the original judgment. The main points of their response are as follows: The appellee's leased houses all have written contracts for those with fixed terms. Those with no fixed term do not. For example, the appellant Hua Ying Pharmacy signed a written contract in the 11th year of the Republic of China, which expired in the 17th year of the Republic of China and was not renewed. This is proof that a fixed-term lease must be established in writing. None of the appellants hold written documents but dare to claim that there is an oral agreement for a term of 20 years. According to the saying that merchants value good faith, this is truly regrettable. Moreover, looking at Hua Ying Pharmacy, even with a written contract, it was only for six years. Would there be a reason for not signing a written document for twenty years? Pan Yuting is the brother of Jiaping, and his testimony is insufficient. As for the customs recognized by law, they must be obvious, long-standing, and publicly practiced. Now, the appellants argue that the reasons for relocation are limited to arrears of rent, own use, or damage to the house requiring reconstruction, and that old tenants have preferential leasing rights, and that the house cannot be reclaimed otherwise. In fact, there has never been this custom. For decades, the architecture of the Public Concession has been changing day by day, reaching its current state. If there is a custom as claimed by the appellants, it would be impossible to rebuild existing houses. Recently, companies such as Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun, as well as Shenzhou and Dongfang Hotels, etc., are all newly built, and the users are not the landlords, nor can it be said that the original tenants are in arrears of rent. Their original houses were not damaged, nor were they rented by the original tenants. All of these can be said to be counter-evidence of the absence of custom. Moreover, there is a special agreement between the parties that is contrary to custom, that is, the house ticket once indicated that both parties have the right to terminate the contract at any time. Why should they use custom as an excuse, abandon the record of the house ticket, and fail to apply it? (Reasoning) The appellants' main points are two: (1) term; (2) custom. Regarding the fact that the appellee leased the houses in question, all those with agreed terms, such as the former Mao Fu Company (the former tenant of the Nanyang Socks Factory) and the appellant Hua Ying Pharmacy (fixed for six years, which has expired), have signed written contracts. If other tenants have also agreed to a term, totaling 20 years, why would they not write a document? Moreover, the appellants are also willing to automatically increase the rent by an additional 40,000 taels per year, in addition to the original amount of more than 60,000 taels, as a condition to cancel the repossession of the houses. The oral agreement for a term of 20 years is not credible. As for whether there is a custom in Shanghai shops regarding the eviction of houses as claimed by the appellants, the Provisional Court has investigated and adopted local customs when handling cases of shop relocation, recognizing that the landlord's eviction must be for the purpose of reclaiming it for his own use, and that seeking profit through digging is not permitted by custom (such as cases No. 3367, 3802, and 3867 in the General Division of the 17th year). However, it should be thoroughly investigated whether this custom is obvious and commonly practiced, as it is an important point of contention between the two parties. Now, the Shanghai Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association has sent a letter stating that it believes that the custom claimed by the appellants is indeed present and solemnly proves that it is the case, and that if this leasing custom is not recognized, the impact will be significant. The members of the Shanghai Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association are mostly members of the capitalist class, so they can represent the psychology of the majority of people in the Concession. There is considerable proof that this custom is clearly prevalent. Furthermore, judging from the reason and the law, at the beginning of the lease, the landlord has already demanded several months' rent from the tenant and acknowledged that the tenant has spent thousands or tens of thousands of gold on renovations. If they can dig up the lease and give it to someone else at any time, without giving considerable compensation or allowing them to stop business and relocate, it is not forgiving in terms of sentiment and unfair in terms of reason. Since the aforementioned custom does not go against good morals, it should be recognized as valid. Now, the appellants are not in arrears of rent, the house was built less than ten years ago, there is no need for reconstruction, and the appellants have no possibility of continuing to rent after reconstruction and improvement. The eviction is causing the rent and renovation expenses to be wasted. It is difficult to recognize this as legitimate. As for the one-sided record in the house ticket, it is not a deed signed by both parties and is difficult to treat it as a special agreement. Just as the house tickets of each family all contain records prohibiting substitution and subletting, but tenants' substitutions or subletting are commonly practiced, how can one use the words that the contract can be terminated at any time in the house ticket as an excuse, regardless of the tenant's losses, and demand immediate relocation? As for the reply from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, although it is not as solid a proof as that from the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, it does not absolutely deny the aforementioned custom. The court can weigh the circumstances and choose to use it as the basis for the judgment. The original trial did not clearly investigate the customary facts claimed by the appellants and made a relocation judgment hastily, which cannot be maintained. However, the appellant Le Quanchang is not a party in the original trial, and how its interests are related is neither stated in the written statement nor personally presented in court. It is of course unqualified, and the appeal of the appellant should be rejected. Based on the above, the appeal of Le Quanchang is illegal, and the appeal of the other appellants is justified. In accordance with Articles 103 and 12 of the Revised Rules of Civil Procedure of the Mixed Court and Article 203 of the Civil Procedure Regulations, the judgment is as stated in the main text.

The Four Banks Reserve Depository Robbery Case Involves Bank Messengers 144

Chen Sanxing is the Main Culprit in this Case

His Confession Still Tries to Pass the Blame to Others

The Messenger Has Been Bailed Out by the Bank

But Must Be Monitored for All Actions

The preparation treasury of the China & South Sea Bank, the Continental Bank, the Jin Cheng Bank, and the Salt Bank was robbed by bandits, with 46,000 yuan of cash and banknotes stolen. The Lao Zha Police Station has been successively arresting the major male and female criminals involved in the case, with eight people apprehended. Previously, Detective Xie Shuiquan and Investigator Zhao Rongsheng of the General Police Station learned that the main culprit in the case, named Chen Sanxing, was from Suzhou. However, his whereabouts were still unknown. However, his younger brother Chen Aba is currently a tea server at the Oriental Hotel. Therefore, they went to the hotel to arrest Aba, hoping to find out where his brother was hiding. Aba confessed at the police station that several of his brothers knew where Sanxing was hiding, but his eldest brother Chen Biao knew. He also said that Chen Biao lived at No. 14 Beile Road in the French Concession. Detective Yan then contacted the French Police Station to request assistance. The police chief dispatched detectives to go to the address and arrest Chen Biao. He knew the address of his younger brother Sanxing and led Detective Yan, Investigator Zhao, and detectives Jin Guanya, etc., to search for him at No. 382 Yaoshui Lane, Xiaoshadu Road, Hongkou. Chen Sanxing was there and unable to escape. He was arrested without resistance. Because the case was being handled by the Lao Zha Police Station, the three Chen brothers were transferred to the Lao Zha Police Station. After questioning, the police chief released Chen Biao and Chen Aba because they were not involved. Chen Sanxing confessed that he was a lookout during the robbery and that they did not initially know that the preparation treasury of the four banks was sending a large sum of money to the Commercial Bank on the Bund that day. He said that they only went to commit the robbery after the messenger of the Commercial Bank reported it. The police chief then sent Detective Liang Chengyu to the Commercial Bank on the Bund with Chen Sanxing to investigate the names of the messengers who reported the information. The bank ordered all of its messengers to stand in a row for Chen to identify. Chen carefully observed them for a week and pointed out one person, saying that he was the informant. Detective Liang then took him back to the police station. He said that his name was Zhou Zhikang and that he was from Shaoxing. Yesterday morning, he and Chen Sanxing were escorted to the Provisional Court, where Judge Gao Junxiang interrogated them. Ru Baoyi, the police station's lawyer, presented Chen's confession to the court, stating that the thief had confessed at the police station and that he was afraid that he would recant during the next court hearing. He requested that he be questioned first. Judge Gao interrogated Chen Sanxing, who confessed that on the morning of the 13th of this month, he went to the Yihong brothel in the French Concession to ask Yuan Genfa for 40 yuan he owed. He saw Zhou Zhikang, Sanguang, Amao, Yuan Laoda, etc., all whispering in the brothel. He asked Yuan Laoda what Zhou did, and Yuan said that Zhou was a cook at the bank. Later, because Yuan did not return the money he owed, he went to room 24 of the Nanjing Hotel to find Yuan to collect the debt. Yuan gave him 100 yuan. He thought that he only owed 40 yuan and that he was suddenly repaying 100 yuan. He also knew that his behavior was bad, so he expected that this 60 yuan must be ill-gotten gains, so he refused to accept it. However, Yuan was angry and said that if he did not accept the money, he would be unfavorable to him and promised to reward him with another 700 yuan. He then said that their money had just been robbed from the Commercial Bank. Only then did he realize that they were whispering in the brothel that morning, planning the robbery. When questioned, Zhou Zhikang completely denied conspiring with Yuan, etc., in the brothel to commit the robbery. The Commercial Bank also hired a lawyer to go to court to request that Zhou be released on bail. Xie Guangfu, the bank's president, went to the case to state that he was willing to vouch for Zhou to wait for the interrogation outside. There was no concern that he would flee. Judge Gao ordered Chen Sanxing to be detained and Zhou Zhikang to be released on bail by the Commercial Bank. He was ordered to come whenever summoned, and the president of the bank was responsible for monitoring his actions and not allowing him to talk to others.

Murder by Robbers in Eastern Victoria Harbour at Midnight 145

An Unexpected Tragedy for a Modest Family

Loving Money as Life, Shouting for Help

Saying They Were Acquainted Led to Fatal Attack

Two Bullets Resulted in Instant and Tragic Death

The robbery and murder of Zhu Xiaomao took place in Eastern Victoria Harbour near the Water and Electricity Plant in Yinhang District, Hudong, the night before last, at midnight. A special account is provided below.

A Prosperous Family, Coveted by Robbers Zhu Xiaomao was 43 years old and from Baoshan County. His wife, Sun, was also of a similar age. Zhu had neither brothers nor children, only the couple. Their home was an ancestral house in Eastern Victoria Harbour with several acres of farmland for cultivation. Zhu also opened a restaurant in the town, taking care of business in the store every day, leaving his wife at home to farm. Therefore, expenses were saved and productivity was strong, and the family was prosperous, leading to covetousness by robbers.

Cash All Hidden in Pant Belt Pocket After the restaurant closed the day before yesterday, Zhu obtained more than 30 yuan of cash from the market and returned home. After dinner, he talked with his wife for a while, forgetting to hand over the cash to his wife. All the cash was hidden in the pant belt pocket. The villagers rested early, and soon the couple closed the door and went to sleep, traveling in the land of sweet dreams.

Robbers Arrive at Midnight, Couple Bound By midnight, the door was pounded like a drum, waking the Zhu couple. Sensing something was wrong, they dared not open the door. Zhu, because he had more than 30 yuan, tied his pant belt around his body to avoid being robbed. Unexpectedly, the door was opened, and two people entered, while others were still outside. The Zhu couple, seeing that the people who came were not good, kept silent. The bandits then plundered, obtaining only five or six pieces of clothing. The place where the cash was hidden was not found. The bandits seemed to know well that Zhu had money on him and robbed him of his pant belt. Zhu, loving money as life, struggled desperately and shouted for help. The bandits were angry and bound the Zhu couple separately, first taking away Zhu's pant belt for further extortion of money.

Two Shots Fired, Tragic Scream and Death At this time, Zhu, seeing that the money was being robbed, looked closely at the two bandits and said, "I recognize you. Why are you so urgent to force me?" The bandits, hearing this, immediately looked alarmed, drew their guns, and fired at Zhu to silence him. One bullet flew out and struck Zhu's buttocks, passing through. Zhu was wounded and fell to the ground, and the second bullet struck the back of his head, causing him to scream tragically and die in a pool of blood. The bandits, seeing that a blood crime had been committed, stopped searching and left.

Crying and Screaming Beside the Corpse After the bandits left, Zhu's wife, Sun, cried and screamed beside the corpse. Neighbors heard the sound and rushed over. Because it was in the countryside, far from the police station, they released her from her bonds and reported to the Yishiertu neighborhood chief, Xu Jiabin, who rushed to investigate and reported to the relevant police station, which immediately sent officers to search. The bandits had already gone far away. The police asked about the appearance and accent of the robbers in order to pursue them.

Court Inquest and Wanted for Murder Yesterday morning, the neighborhood chief Xu Jiabin submitted a statement to the local court for an inquest. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Liu and Coroner Xuan and others arrived at the scene and confirmed that the deceased Zhu Xiaomao had indeed died of gunshot wounds during his lifetime. They ordered the corpse to be collected and sent separate letters to various agencies to issue a warrant for the arrest of the murderers, so that they could be brought to justice.

Judgment in the Case Against Deng Zhongze 146

The case against Deng Zhongze, the general supervisor of the Fuan Life Insurance Company, who was previously accused of fraud by Liu Yulin, Shen Shulin, Zhang Fuqing, etc., was heard in the Provisional Court. Deng also filed a counterclaim against Deng Wenhai, Wu Hanzhou, Wu Shutang, etc., accusing them of false accusations. After many trials, there were no less than fifty or sixty plaintiffs and defendants, and more than thirty lawyers, including He Shiming, He Xianzhang, Qu Yue, and Yao Jian. As a result, this case has attracted much attention. The judgment was rendered on March 6, and Deng Zhongze was found not guilty. The original judgment is transcribed below:

"Main Text" Deng Zhongze is not guilty. The part of the civil lawsuit attached by the plaintiff is transferred to the Civil Division of this court for trial. Deng Wenhai, Wu Hanzhou, and Wu Shutang are not guilty.

"Facts" Deng Zhongze was the general supervisor of Fuan Insurance and Warehouse Co., Ltd. The company was established in the 27th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, with its headquarters located on Des Voeux Road, Hong Kong, and registered with the Hong Kong government. In the 32nd year of Guangxu, a branch was established at No. 51 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. In the 4th year of the Republic of China, the Hong Kong Fuan headquarters also handled life insurance and deposited a security deposit of 22,000 pounds with the British government in accordance with British insurance regulations. In the 5th year of the Republic of China, it registered with the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce in Beijing. In the 14th year of the Republic of China, the Hong Kong Fuan headquarters, due to the lack of development in the life insurance business in Hong Kong, entrusted the Shanghai China Fuan Life Insurance Company to handle the life insurance business. The office of the so-called Fuan Life Insurance Company was located in the office of the Shanghai branch of the Hong Kong Fuan Company at No. 51 Jiangxi Road, and Deng Zhongze was also the general manager. It also independently issued articles of association, which contained the words "The headquarters of China Fuan Life Insurance Company is located in Shanghai." The premium receipts issued to policyholders were sometimes stamped with the seal of China Fuan Company and sometimes with the seal of the Shanghai branch of Hong Kong Fuan Company. In December of the 15th year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai China Fuan Company also believed that there was no hope for the development of the life insurance business and stopped receiving new policyholders. However, it could not immediately seek to end the old policyholders and continued to collect premiums. When old policyholders died, it refunded the policy and paid compensation in accordance with the regulations, amounting to more than 200,000 yuan. In August of the 17th year of the Republic of China, the Hong Kong Fuan Company, due to poor business performance, was resolved by the shareholders' meeting

Page 16

to be liquidated as announced in the newspaper. Luo Zuosheng was appointed to handle the liquidation of the Hong Kong headquarters. Luo Zuosheng then authorized Deng Zhongze to act as the liquidator in Shanghai. In March of the 18th year of the Republic of China, Deng Zhongze appointed the British accountant Yimaoli as the liquidator. Because the Shanghai China Fuan Company published an advertisement in the newspaper in March of the 18th year of the Republic of China, stating that it was operating as usual, it aroused the attention of general policyholders of Hong Kong Fuan Company and Shanghai China Fuan Company, who believed that Deng Zhongze had falsely established China Fuan Company and defrauded them of premiums, and filed lawsuits with this court on charges of fraud and attached civil lawsuits, requesting the court to order the defendant Deng Zhongze to repay the premiums already paid by the plaintiffs. During the trial, Deng Zhongze argued that among the accusers, Wu Hanzhou and Wu Shutang's policies had already expired, and that Deng Wenhai's policy had been signed by himself and there was no room for dispute. They had fabricated facts and intended for others to be subjected to criminal punishment, which constituted the crime of false accusation. Therefore, he filed a counterclaim, requesting a joint judgment from the court. (To be continued)

Gathering a Group of Women to Make a Scene in the Auditorium

Negotiating a Three-Chapter Law Through Friends' Mediation

Former Lover Pretends to Be Younger Brother 150

Unexpectedly Sharing a Bed

And Then Fleeing Behind Her Husband's Back

Gu Liusheng, a man from Yangzhou residing at No. 140 Gonghe Xin Road in Zhabei, engages in the used goods business. He is over thirty years old, and his wife, Madam Fan, is thirty-two years old and quite beautiful. They have been married for several years and their relationship is still harmonious. At first, Gu was completely unaware, but as time passed, he noticed their excessive intimacy and suspicions arose. Husband and Wife Granted Separate Residence 151

Jin Junde, a Taoist priest from Beixin Jing in the northwest of the district, hired lawyer Lu Ruizheng to file a lawsuit in the local court against his wife, Zhu Qiuyun, accusing her of insulting elders, being unruly, and making it impossible to live together, requesting a divorce. The defendant, Zhu Qiuyun, also hired lawyer Wang Chengkuan to present a defense, stating that the plaintiff had an affair with a woman named Xiufang while away from home, abandoning her and already having two sons and one daughter with the other woman. Therefore, she refused to divorce and requested to live together. This case had been heard twice without resolution, and the court ordered them to reconcile out of court. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Zhenhai held a continued hearing. Both parties, accompanied by their lawyers, appeared in court. The judge briefly questioned both parties, and as a result, they reached an agreement to live separately. The plaintiff will pay the defendant a monthly living allowance of six yuan. The two boys (one seven years old, one four years old) will be raised by the plaintiff, and the ten-year-old girl will be raised by the defendant. The judge also stated in the settlement record that if the plaintiff fails to fulfill the agreement, the defendant may apply for enforcement, and the costs incurred shall be borne by the plaintiff. Both parties were satisfied, signed the agreement, and left the court.

Unable to Execute Due to Person Missing

Shen Dianru, a graduate of Wuben Girls' School, subsequently entered Bethel School and is now enrolled in Tongde Obstetrics School. Young Woman Accuses Husband of Abuse and Requests Separate Residence 153

One Week Given to Reconcile Out of Court

A young woman, Tang Zhou (also known as Zhou Guizhen), recently hired lawyer Lu Qi to file a lawsuit in the local court against her husband, Tang Wenhong (also known as Wenhong), claiming that living together was unbearable and requesting separate residence to avoid accidents and protect her integrity. Her statement essentially stated that in March of last year, she married the defendant through a matchmaker. Initially, the defendant pretended to be attentive and tried every means to accumulate her small savings because he saw she had some wealth. Later, he demanded clothing and jewelry, which he pawned and squandered. Eventually, when the money was gone, his love waned, and he began to give her cold looks every day. He soon became angry and frequently resorted to violence, treating her like an enemy. All of the plaintiff's clothing and cash had been pawned and squandered by the defendant. She had been repeatedly beaten and insulted, leaving her with scars all over her body. The marital relationship was almost like ice and charcoal. The relationship between husband and wife should be based on kindness and righteousness, and gender equality is clearly stipulated in the policies of the National Government. However, the defendant's treatment of the plaintiff has been one of abuse in every way, as described above, which not only goes against the original intention of the marriage but is also not tolerated by law and reason. For the sake of her own future, the plaintiff could have filed for divorce, but out of respect for etiquette and a reluctance to violate the principle of "remaining faithful from beginning to end," she has endured insults and made concessions in all matters. However, the defendant has taken this as an advantage and has instead driven the plaintiff back to her mother's home, neglecting her livelihood. Having no other choice, she entrusted a lawyer to send a letter to the defendant, proposing separate residence in order to preserve her safety. However, the defendant is cunning and stubborn and has ignored it. If the plaintiff were to live with him, not only would the abuse be unbearable, but the wicked mother-in-law would also assist in the abuse, making it even harder to be a wife. If the days were long and peaceful, her elderly mother's livelihood would be difficult, and she would not be able to continue living off her savings. Moreover, her mother is old and frail, and they depend on each other. In addition, the plaintiff is pregnant and awaiting childbirth, and funds are urgently needed. After much consideration, she has no choice but to seek justice and legal sanctions to ensure her survival. The defendant, Tang Wenhong, also hired lawyer Cai Jishi to present a defense, requesting to live together, claiming that the plaintiff had falsely accused him of abuse in an attempt to divorce. He stated that in March of last year, he married Zhou Guizhen, the daughter of Zhou Ziqin, through matchmakers such as Chen Kuilin, Tang Zhang, and others. After the marriage, the plaintiff could not endure the hard work of the old-fashioned family and complained at every turn. She was often extravagant and frequently went to amusement parks with her girlfriends. The defendant's monthly salary of twenty yuan was not enough to cover her expenses. His mother advised her, but she refused to change. His mother treated the plaintiff as if she were her own daughter, showering her with love and care, and there was no abuse. He requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed and that she be ordered to live together. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang held a hearing. The plaintiff, Tang Zhou, testified that she was twenty years old, from Wuxi, and living at her mother's home at No. 7 Siwei North Lane, Wangjiazhai Road, Zhabei. She also described the events that had occurred and claimed that the defendant had other women outside, which made it unbearable for her. The defendant, Tang Wenhong, testified that he was twenty-four years old, from Wuxi, and living at No. 10, Lane 2, Tianbao Lane, Xinjiang Road, Zhabei. He worked at the Jiangxi Road Water Company and earned a monthly salary of twenty-four yuan. He claimed that the plaintiff's lawsuit was completely fabricated. The judge attempted to reconcile the parties in court, advising the plaintiff to live with the defendant. However, the plaintiff refused, so the judge advised the plaintiff to stay at the home of the defendant's relatives for a few days, and then live together again when both parties were calm. Both parties expressed their willingness to do so. However, the plaintiff specified that she wanted to stay at the home of the defendant's aunt in Suzhou for half a year and that she would be due to give birth in September of this year, requesting that the defendant pay her ten yuan per month for expenses. The defendant replied that he only earned a salary of twenty-four yuan per month and that even household expenses were sometimes insufficient, so he had no extra money to squander. He could only afford to pay one or two yuan per month. The judge repeatedly advised both parties, and as a result, the defendant agreed to pay nine yuan per month for six months. The judge was about to have the settlement record drawn up and have both parties sign it when the plaintiff suddenly raised five conditions: (1) The defendant must pay her ten yuan per month; (2) The defendant must return all of the plaintiff's clothes; (3) The defendant must redeem the plaintiff's clothes that he had pawned in the past; (4) The defendant must also redeem the gold jewelry that he had pawned, and return the plaintiff's private savings of over one hundred yuan; (5) If the defendant still abuses her, the plaintiff is allowed to file another lawsuit. The judge, finding the plaintiff unreasonable, ordered the lawyers of both parties to reconcile out of court. If they cannot reach a settlement within a week, another hearing will be held.

Brothel Prostitutes Harass Customers, Affecting Wonton Vendor 155

Since the authorities of the Public Concession strictly prohibited prostitution, most of the Yangzhou brothels have relocated. As the French Concession has licenses available for the flower tax, the majority have moved there and continue their lives as prostitutes. The areas with the most brothels are the East and West Zilaihuo Streets, Caishi Street, Qianxin Street, and the vicinity of the Great World. Every night, after the electric lights are turned on, the various street corners and alley entrances are filled with women, all clamoring and crowding the streets. Their white faces and dark eyebrows are almost blinding. Pedestrians who pass through the area are often dragged and pulled by these women. If they encounter a naive person from the countryside, they will even carry the person into the brothel, forcing them to sit in a room and stay the night. Those who enter their doors must spend at least five or six small yuan or even one yuan before being released. Therefore, respectable businessmen avoid these areas at night. The Chamber of Commerce and other organizations have repeatedly sent letters to the police, requesting strict action. On the evening of the 25th, around 11 PM, a young man named Jia (approximately 20 years old), who had just arrived in Shanghai from the countryside, was wearing a flat-topped melon-skin satin hat, a blue bamboo cloth cotton robe, and a small western-style satin vest. He spoke with a Changshu accent and appeared to be a farmer from the countryside. He was walking on East Zilaihuo Street when he saw more than a dozen prostitutes from Ruifu Lane dragging and pulling customers in the middle of the road. Jia stopped to stare. The prostitutes, seeing that he was a country bumpkin, immediately went forward to drag him. Several prostitutes and pimps grabbed Jia's hands and lifted his feet, as if they were kidnapping him, intending to drag him inside. Jia was terrified and shouted for help. The prostitutes released him, and Jia, seeing that the prostitutes had let him go, ran out of the alley and into the street. Unfortunately, he bumped into a wonton stand parked at the entrance of the lane, causing it to overturn. All of the iron pots and bowls were smashed, and the wrapped wontons and fresh noodles were scattered everywhere. The owner of the stand grabbed Jia and demanded ten yuan in compensation. A large crowd gathered to watch. Jia, seeing that he had caused the accident, was terrified and his face turned pale. He only had one large yuan and twelve small yuan on him. The owner of the stand insisted on taking his clothes as collateral, but Jia refused, and tears streamed down his face. The onlookers, feeling sorry for him, criticized the prostitutes for dragging pedestrians, which had caused the accident. They ordered the prostitutes to pay three yuan and collected sixteen small yuan from the onlookers. Together with Jia's one large yuan and twelve small yuan, they gave it to the wonton vendor. A small commotion was finally settled. Jia, ashamed, headed south toward Shanghai.

Postal Rates Temporarily Postponed 160

The General Post Office received instructions from the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating: "For the information of all concerned, the case of the Railway Department requesting to send personnel to discuss and revise postal rates has been discussed. Director Pan Discusses Pharmaceutical Mediation Case 161

Most Decisions Based on Legal Mediation

Those Who Disagree Can Apply for Arbitration

Although the pharmaceutical dispute has been mediated, it is not completely resolved. Hu Qingyu and Cai Tongde are still closed. A Wuchen News reporter interviewed Director Pan Gongzhan of the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday and conducted the following interview: (Q) The pharmaceutical capitalists claim that this case was a biased decision by your bureau, is that true? (A) This case was initially about the employment of unemployed workers. Our bureau was ordered by the municipal government to mediate. Subsequently, the employees in the industry declared a strike, demanding that the capitalists hire more workers due to the heavy workload. Our bureau then legally convened a labor-capital mediation committee, which made an impartial decision. (Q) How is the mediation committee organized? (A) According to law, for each dispute, the government agency appoints one to three members, and the labor and capital sides each appoint two representatives. The mediation committee in this case was composed of one representative each from our bureau, the municipal party headquarters, and the Public Security Bureau, along with two representatives each from the labor and capital sides. (Q) The capitalists advertised that their representatives did not attend the meeting, can a decision be made in that case? (A) This case was formally mediated on the 21st with all members present. The capitalists' representatives, Zhuang Meitang and Zhang Zhihao, legally attended, but they insisted on their views regarding the hiring of additional workers. At 10 PM, no decision had been reached, and it was agreed to continue the meeting on the 24th to resolve the matter. All representatives signed the decision, including Zhuang and Zhang. Therefore, the mediation on the 24th was a continuation and not another meeting. Furthermore, the Pharmaceutical Association submitted a petition to our bureau on the 23rd, stating that the representatives of the association could only insist on the original agreement during tomorrow's mediation. It was resolved to stop sending representatives to attend and wait for the bureau's decision before applying for arbitration. Our bureau forwarded the original petition to the mediation committee for review. The mediation committee was a collegial body and made decisions based on majority vote. Since the original petition requested a decision and was prepared to apply for arbitration, a decision could be made with the consent of five members. Therefore, this decision was not inappropriate. However, since the capitalists' representatives did not sign, they could apply to the municipal government for arbitration within five days. The capitalists' representatives had already been nominated and reported, and their names could not be crossed out simply because they did not sign. The claim that this decision was a unilateral decision by our bureau is a fundamental misunderstanding. The Pharmaceutical Association's advertisement even stated that "there is no reason to request the bureau to make a prompt decision." It should be noted that the original petition from the association on the 23rd is on file, and there is no room for denial. (Q) How did your bureau handle the case after the mediation committee made a decision? (A) Our bureau believes that this case has been delayed for too long, affecting people's lives and public order. It is not appropriate for both sides to continue arguing. Therefore, we ordered the Pharmaceutical Association and the Workers' Union to comply with the decision and resume work and business on the 25th. We heard that Hu Qingyu and Cai Tongde have not yet reopened, and we have ordered them to comply. (Q) Does this decision conflict with the Central Party Headquarters' approval of the Pharmaceutical Qin Association and the municipal government's directive to prioritize the employment of unemployed workers? (A) The mediation committee is responsible for the decisions made. Those who disagree can apply for arbitration according to law, and the reasonableness of the decision will be determined by the arbitration ruling. However, according to my personal observation, the Central Party Headquarters' approval and the municipal government's directive consistently instructed pharmaceutical companies to find ways to prioritize the employment of these unemployed workers. This does not mean that pharmaceutical companies should not hire them at all. The terms "prioritize" and "find ways" show that the Central and Municipal Governments were concerned about the plight of unemployed workers and wanted to find ways to employ them first, even if it was impossible. Now that there are legal ways to do so, the reasons for the mediation decision are indeed based on this point. On the one hand, according to the survey, larger pharmacies have thriving businesses and slow dispensing, which necessitates hiring additional workers for the sake of patients. On the other hand, in accordance with the Central and Municipal Governments' intentions, pharmaceutical companies are responsible for prioritizing the employment of qualified unemployed workers. The people previously placed by the Workers' Union are treated separately, either employed or given severance pay and sent back to their hometowns. It seems that there is no conflict. In all fairness, Chinese pharmacies are often too busy, and dispensing is delayed for three or four hours, which is common. Most patients feel this pain. Adding workers to remedy this would be what society hopes for.

Shanghai Treasure Stamp Tax Bureau Schedules Regular Inspections of Business Account Books 162

Personnel to Be Dispatched on April 1

The Shanghai Treasure Stamp Tax Branch notes that the use of stamps on business account books and receipts is becoming increasingly popular, but many ignorant merchants do not pay attention to it, and there are also many who intend to evade taxes. Any business account books, receipts, etc., that are found not to have stamps affixed will be punished in accordance with the regulations. Impersonating Salesman to Cheat People 164

Blind Man Out of Luck

Qian Heming, a man from Pudong, is forty-two years old and has been blind since childhood. Therefore, he learned fortune-telling to support himself. He also set up a fortune-telling shop at No. 21 Zixia Road, outside the Dadongmen, and his business was doing well. Yesterday afternoon around 3 PM, a man named Jia came to Qian's shop and claimed to be a salesman in a rice shop, selling rice to him. If he wanted it, the price could be cheaper. Qian, seeing that his family's rice was running out, negotiated a price with Jia and ordered one dan of rice. Jia hurriedly left and then went to the Cuichunxiang Rice Shop in Gaoxiangtou, outside the Xiaonanmen, and said that he lived at No. 21 Zixia Road and asked them to send one dan of white rice immediately, saying that he would take them there and pay the rice price after it was delivered. The shop did not doubt him and sent a porter, Cai Yaodong, to deliver the rice, following Jia to the address. Jia told Qian that the rice had arrived. Qian, hearing this, ordered the porter to pour the rice into the rice jar and then handed 19 yuan to Jia for the rice. Jia suddenly had an idea and asked the porter to send another dan of rice from the shop to the same place, saying that the rice price could be calculated together. Cai agreed and returned to the shop, sending another dan of rice to the same place. However, Jia was no longer there. So he delivered the rice to Qian. At this time, Qian was very surprised and said that he only needed one dan of rice, why send two? Cai said that if the rice sent later was not needed, it could be returned, but the price of the one dan of rice sent earlier should be paid to him. Qian found the matter even more strange and loudly said that the rice money had already been taken by your salesman. Cai said that there was no salesman in his shop and accused Qian of deliberately denying the rice money. Therefore, they disagreed and had a big conflict. Huang Xiaokun, the guard of the 14th post, heard about it and rushed to the scene, inquired about the situation, and brought them both back to the First District Headquarters. They were ordered to be detained temporarily pending investigation and preliminary examination.

Resignation of Dock Supervisor 165

Zhou Linhe, a Chinese employee in charge of the Zhanghuabang Haikai River Dock Office in Songnan, is 59 years old and a native of Zhanghuabang. He entered customs at the age of 22 and has been there for 37 years. He is very familiar with managing the flag raising, navigation of ships, and security matters at Gaoqiao, Zhanghuabang, Paotaiwan, and Bailonggang in Pudong. He is also proficient in English and highly respected by successive Deputy River Dock Commissioners. He has gained considerable insights into the research of various scales regarding ship routes, tides, and storms. He also had two exclusive duties: (1) Based on years of experience, he could detect the arrival of hurricanes several hours before a storm broke out. Upon detection, he would immediately report to the Shanghai River Dock Office via telephone, notifying all flag stations along the Yangtze River to raise storm warning signals, warning ships en route to avoid danger. (2) He calculated the tidal ebb and flow chart for the solar calendar based on the lunar calendar from years of experience (Western name: "Tide Table"). This chart had to be prepared and sent to Shanghai one month in advance. For example, information such as the ebb and flow times and scale changes for each day from May 1st to the end of May had to be sent in mid-April so that the Customs, River Dock Office, and shipowners could consult it and have a grasp of the situation. Now, Mr. Zhou has submitted his resignation due to the Customs regulations stipulating a service period of only 35 years, which he has exceeded. It has been approved and will take effect on April 1st.

Publication of Judicial Regulations of the National Government 168

Since the establishment of the National Government in Guangzhou on July 1, 1925, a considerable number of laws have been created and revised over the past five years. Although books such as "Complete Collection of Laws and Regulations" and "Compilation of Laws and Regulations" have been published in the market, they mostly focus on administrative laws and regulations and are difficult for legal professionals to consult. In order to ensure that the people of the country understand the law and to facilitate the participation of legal professionals in government affairs, the Judicial Yuan of the National Government has specially compiled a book titled "Judicial Regulations of the National Government." All currently effective judicial laws, regulations, orders, and explanatory documents have been included without omission. The contents are divided into ten categories: Party Affairs, Official System, Official Regulations, Trial, Civil, Criminal, Administrative, Laws and Regulations, Judicial Administration, Foreign Affairs, and Miscellaneous Records, with further detailed chapters. The system is detailed and the printing is exquisite. The entire book consists of two volumes, totaling over 2,000 pages, and is priced at six yuan, plus four jiao for postage for outside areas. It is now being sold by the Gazette Office of the Secretariat of the Judicial Yuan. Those who want to understand the law must have a copy at hand.

Ancient Edition of the Twenty-Four Histories to be Available for Pre-Order 169

Published by the Commercial Press

In 1920, the Commercial Press compiled and printed the "Sibu Congkan." Because good editions of the official histories were not available, they were omitted. For more than ten years, extensive efforts have been made to find them. Except for the "History of Yuan," which used the Ming edition, and the "History of Ming," which used the Qing edition, old Song and Yuan editions have been collected for the rest, named "Hundred Patch Edition of the Twenty-Four Histories" to correct many errors and omissions in the palace edition. It is reported that ancient editions of various histories have been collected by the publishing house, and samples have been produced. Pre-orders will begin in early next month and the photo-printed edition will be published.

Relatives and friends have been visiting him morning and night. According to the doctor, the dangerous period has completely passed, and he will be able to return to work in about two weeks.

British-American Tobacco Workers' Union: Sent a telegram to express condolences to the workers of the British-American Tobacco Factory in Qingdao, which reads: "To the entire Executive Committee of the Qingdao British-American Tobacco Factory Union, via the Qingdao General Labor Union: We have read in the newspaper that Cao Yunxiang, advisor to the Shanghai British-American Tobacco Factory, went to Qingdao and, after negotiating with the factory owner, decided to suddenly suspend work starting on the 19th. We are extremely indignant upon hearing this. According to previous reports, your union workers demanded that the factory increase wages, with male workers receiving an increase of two jiao and female workers receiving an increase of one jiao. After struggling, you finally won. However, not long after, troubles have arisen again. It is understandable that imperialist capitalists oppress workers, but Cao Yunxiang's decision to suspend the factory and resist the workers is an act of servility and a willingness to please foreigners, which is inexcusable. Cao was known for instigating animosity between labor and management and undermining the labor movement when he was at the Shanghai factory. We have previously warned him on record. However, he dares to continue his evil ways and is now oppressing our Qingdao factory workers with bloody hands. His reactionary intentions are not only condemned by the people of the country but are also intolerable to nature. Our union shares the same cause and feels the pain together. We cannot stand idly by. In addition to leading more than 8,000 workers to support your union and severely warning Cao Yunxiang, we are sending this telegram to express our condolences. We hope that your union will uphold the fearless spirit of the General Manager, strive to fight against evil forces, and be assured of ultimate victory. Please provide us with the true situation so that we can provide support. We eagerly await your response."

Pawnshop Workers' Union: Held its eighth regular meeting yesterday. (1) Report (omitted). Matters discussed and resolved: (1) The Civil Training Committee has not yet issued a certificate of registration to this union. How to handle this matter? (Resolved) Resubmit to the Civil Training Committee, requesting that it be issued to facilitate the labor movement. (2) The case of a vacancy at the Baotai pawnshop. According to a letter from the manager, the position is important, and the pawnshop employees are not capable enough to be promoted. How should this union handle this matter? (Resolved) Reply to the group, attach the original letter from the employer, and send a representative to the union to explain the situation clearly before deciding how to proceed. (3) Member Du Baoxun lost his membership card and requested that it be declared invalid. (Resolved) Lost membership badges will be declared invalid in the monthly publication, and a new card will be issued. This matter will be handled by the Organization Section. (4) Cases of various groups refusing to pay fees. (Resolved) For those who have received membership badges, the Accounting Section will send personnel to actively collect the fees. (2) For those who have not received membership badges, this matter will be handled by the Organization Section. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

A Laughing Matter 175

— Seafarer

A: Do you have any poor relatives?

B: I always pretend not to know them.

A: Then do you have any rich relatives?

B: They always pretend not to know me.

Wife: Don't forget today. Bring back a pound of butter, two pounds of lard, and a bottle of chili oil.

Husband: Oh dear. Why do you only want oily things? I'm afraid they'll slip right out of my head in a moment and I won't remember.

Husband (rushing into the police station): Quick, lock me up! Quick, lock me up! I just hit my wife with my cane.

Police officer: Did you hit her vital spot and kill her?

Wife: No, but he's chasing me closely and is about to kill me!

Old pastor: All good people will go to a place after they die. There are jade pillars and gold-paved floors. It's more magnificent and comfortable than anything else. What's the name of this place? Do you all know?

All the elementary school students: The movie theater!

A: Lao Bing is as honest as they come. He doesn't want a single penny.

B: That's right. He needs tens of thousands to be satisfied.

Snake Oddities 176

— Zhang Juping

There are countless kinds of snakes, all wonderfully strange. However, they are mostly found in the humid and hot areas of the south. In our Suzhou area, they are quite simple. The villagers are familiar with and can name only three kinds: the green whip snake, the red-banded snake, and the earth viper. The red-banded snake and the earth viper are both viviparous and highly venomous, especially the earth viper. Those bitten by it often face life-threatening danger if not treated properly. The green whip snake, on the other hand, is oviparous and has very little venom. Initially, the bite also causes redness, swelling, and pain, but it subsides the next day and does not cause harm. This snake has the characteristic of living in people's houses. It can use spaces under the floorboards, between walls, and under tiles as its burrows. Because its body has protection, it does not come into contact with wind, sun, rain, or dew. Its green exterior gradually turns into a dull grayish-white. Also, because it is accustomed to living with people, it loses its inherent fear and often appears calmly in front of people. Villagers call it the "house-guarding snake" and bless it with good intentions, not daring to kill it, believing that killing it will bring great disaster. This is simply due to superstition.

Years ago, my family demolished an old, long-abandoned stove. Inside the stove, we found more than a dozen snake eggs. The snakes had already hatched and left, leaving only the eggshells. The quality of the shells was different from ordinary chicken and duck eggs. They were soft and pliable, much like silkworm cocoons, and were also made up of fine threads, but more loosely woven. The most peculiar thing was that the dozen or so eggs were naturally connected in a string. Each egg was separated from the others by two or three fen (a unit of length). A tube as thick as a reed stem was attached between them. The tube was hollow and connected to the egg, and its material was the same as the eggshell. Examining the entire structure, it was seamless. Only the top of the first egg had a small hole. Presumably, the dozen or so small snakes emerged from this hole, and the tubes were their passageways. Such a strange egg shape is indeed unique among living things.

Recently, I have been working at the Shipping Association. During the long, boring nights, I often chat with the tea server, Bingchang. Bingchang is from Nantong. He said that in his hometown, a farmer named Jia woke up one morning to use the toilet. He saw something wriggling next to the toilet. Upon closer inspection, it was a snake. The front part of its body was already in a crack in the wall, leaving only its tail exposed. It was about a foot long. Jia quickly grabbed and pulled it, but it wouldn't move. He exerted more force, and it suddenly snapped in two. Jia threw the tail away and told his family. This eventually reached the ears of a neighbor, an old man, who came over and said to Jia, "If a snake is cut off above the third segment of its tail, it will inevitably die soon, even if it manages to escape at the time. However, if it is cut off below the third segment, it can still live and its venom will be ten times that of a normal snake, and it will seek revenge. Let's go take a look." Jia then showed him the snake's tail. The old man said, "Oh, it's only two segments. It certainly won't die. You should be prepared from now on." Jia was worried upon hearing this and was constantly on guard. After four or five years, nothing happened, and his mind was somewhat at ease. One night, just as he was going to bed, he tucked his mosquito net tightly under the quilt, also as a precaution against snakes. Unexpectedly, a tiny slit opened up in the top of the net. A snake somehow squeezed through the slit. Its whole body had passed through, but the severed end had formed a fleshy ball that could not fit through the slit, putting it in a bind. It flailed wildly. Jia woke up in surprise. Upon realizing that it was a snake, he prepared to wait. After a long time, it did not come down. He looked outside the net and saw the fleshy ball. He then knew that the snake was helpless. Taking advantage of its being suspended in the air, it died. This is because snakes can only move forward and cannot retreat.

Family Little Knowledge 177

— Lubing

When washing silk fabrics, adding a little salt to the water beforehand can make the material shiny and less prone to fading.

After cooking fish in a pot, it often leaves a fishy smell. Washing it with cold water and a spoonful of vinegar will remove it.

Silverware stored in boxes easily tarnishes when exposed to humid air. Sprinkling starch on top when storing them will keep them looking like new even after a long time.

The best way to brush away stains on leather sofas is to first add some ammonia to warm water, dip a soft cloth in it and wipe, and then wipe with a dry cloth.

Anecdotes from the Wedding of Zeng Yangfu and Feng Xiaoyun 178

— Lichen

The wedding of Zeng Yangfu, Deputy Director of the Construction Committee, and Miss Feng Xiaoyun, sister of Feng Yifei, Director of the Preparatory Office of the Central Military Training Corps, was held at 4:00 p.m. on the 22nd at the auditorium of the Capital Artillery Standard Lizhi Society. It was a grand occasion. Here are some interesting details:

Perfect Arrangement: Both parties appointed responsible personnel in advance to arrange everything at the Lizhi Society. The auditorium was filled with congratulatory banners and couplets. A ceremonial table was set up on the stage, and flower baskets were placed densely. The exterior of the hall was also covered with colorful cloth, which was eye-catching. Other facilities such as the newlyweds' rest room and the guests' rest room were all prepared. Someone said, "The groom is the Deputy Director of the Construction Committee. This arrangement is only the smallest part of the construction. In the future, the two parties will cooperate, and the results of the construction will be considerable." Everyone who heard this applauded.

Interesting Congratulatory Messages: Banners were the most numerous among the gifts, numbering about hundreds. The inscriptions were all pedantic. Only "Yu Bailing, Building the Foundation" was relatively relevant. Among them, Chen Guofu's congratulatory message was the most interesting. It is recorded below. "Construction is difficult, and marrying a wife is even more difficult. Yangfu has come to this day after planning for ten years. I was entrusted to be the matchmaker, searching everywhere but finding no suitable match. Limited to girls from Suzhou and Huzhou, their physiques were incompatible. Their temperaments were gentle and their faces were beautiful. Their character and learning had to be high. With all the appropriate conditions met, how could there be a lady who could match this man? Today, I entrusted friends, and tomorrow, I'll search myself. From Tianjin, I searched to America. From America, I turned back. Guangzhou for several months yielded nothing. Nanjing and Shanghai were fruitless. Joining the army and the Northern Expedition were in vain. Returning from Pingjin, I only sighed. The days passed by. Helplessly, the matchmakers were all ineffective. Liver fire raged, and the stomach was ill. Groaning on the bed, the doctor advised to start a family early. I asked my old mother and consulted with friends, redoubling my efforts, and finally achieved today's marriage. Originally, Miss Feng Xiaoyun's talent was commensurate, as passionate as Yangfu. Regretting meeting too late, ambitions are finally achieved. Respecting and loving each other, no need to talk about any clauses. Once it's decided, there's no need to ask God's permission. Love is originally an electrical attraction. Marriage is for building a new family. A new family, just created, should set an example of thrift. Believe that human effort is omnipotent. Let's all raise a glass and congratulate this happy couple." The language was extremely humorous and interesting, a unique approach to congratulatory messages. Zhang Wuhua's couplet was "Golden fortune unites hearts, good to take advantage of the spring breeze to create a marriage contract. The society can inspire ambition, elegant to abstain from the dawn and cock crow." The local scenery also contained elegance and fun. Dai Jitao's double happiness character, written on Panlong paper, decorated with a gold-edged frame, was truly a special feature.

Venerable Wu's Admonition: Venerable Wu and Zhang Jingjiang were both the officiants. Venerable Wu delivered the admonition, mainly saying that Comrade Yangfu had been working for the revolution for many years and had recently been striving for construction. It was heard that the newlyweds Yangfu would take a honeymoon to the United States to study construction work. Congratulations, congratulations. He also hoped that they would work hard to build their family and have many descendants.

Director Feng's Embarrassment: Feng Yifei wore a military uniform and the Baoding Medal, escorting his sister into the auditorium with small, piano-like steps. Feng was not used to it and was greatly embarrassed. Feng had once served as the commander of the 22nd Route Army and was usually lively and brave when commanding soldiers. Now, being suddenly restrained in this way, it was no wonder that his face was red. The observers even called out "The Director is embarrassed!", which made Feng even more uneasy.

Wan Hua's Honors in America (Part 1) 179

— Han

Mei Lanfang's Portrait in the New York Evening Post

Before Wan Hua went to America, many people were worried for him. However, I knew that the American reception depended entirely on the effectiveness of the publicity. If Americans could vigorously promote him, all kinds of difficulties could be easily solved. And now it has come true. A friend sent me a large bundle of news about Mr. Mei from New York. Among them were lengthy articles, a dazzling array. The newspapers included the New York Evening Post, the New York Times, the New York Sun, and the New York Public Opinion Post. I will make the effort to abridge and translate these articles to satisfy readers. I believe that not only theater enthusiasts will have the pleasure of seeing them first, but also those who care about national affairs will be pleased to see the foreigners' comments on the excellence of Chinese art.

Mr. Shirwin, a reporter for the New York Evening Post, wrote a long article. I will excerpt and translate the following: (The following is an overview of the essay)

Judging from the enthusiastic applause of the audience at the Forty-Ninth Street Theater last night, I predict that the entire city of New York will soon be overwhelmed by a craze for the Chinese people and Chinese things. Therefore, I dare to bet all that I have and assert that the most curious people in New York will abandon their black nightclubs and turn to worship Eastern art. At the same time, there will also be a large number of half-baked, pretentious, and self-proclaimed Chinese scholars appearing in the halls of hotels.

This further proves that publicity in theaters, if properly executed, will be one of the most surprising forms of international propaganda.

Isn't it even more credible that the American Chinese Society invited Mr. Mei to come here? I also know that within a week, people in New York will be talking about the Chinese and Chinese things, arousing our sympathy for the Chinese to an incredible degree. This kind of craze has swept the city several times before. The Spanish once, the blacks again, and now it is the era of the Chinese.

European Travel Correspondence (47) 180

— Liu Haisu

André Derain (2)

Since the end of the European War, he has often studied the works of the great masters of the past in the Louvre. Towards their passionate paintings, he gradually became fond of Renoir's precise structure and Corot's lyrical genius. All other aspects of Corot were also appreciated by him. The so-called poetry, feeling, freshness, and stability of method. However, the entire Louvre was very intimate to Derain. Chardin and his still lifes, Claude Lorrain and his trees, Rubens' roughness, Courbet and Manet's interesting whites, the spirit of light and all the dazzling fantasies, all the artificial "light and dark", all the brave and noble Arabian styles. This kind of resource, classified in a dictatorial way, enabled him to rediscover the objective world. Renoir's sensual, trembling women, the gorgeous background arrangements, the vivid landscapes, and the enchanting colors, in short, that power of life written with noble sources. His reddish-brown and emerald green palette provided some workable oiliness, which displayed the immortal traces of his delicate backgrounds and gorgeous foregrounds. This is a synthesis of all charms. It flows out casually, making his art so sympathetic.

Derain is a learned figure. The rationale he practices can generally be said to be Esoteric (secretly transmitted). The paintings of past masters are all inexplicable secrets in his eyes. In fact, in his view, art is nothing more than the mystery of "great" "power". His curiosity is always eager to move, continuing his impassioned exploration. Those who only seek in his works a ridiculous imitation of the traces of the masters' paintings will ridicule him and despise him. There are still many people who are moved by the alluring solemnity on his canvases and express great respect for him. Derain is a mystic, a sensualist, and a refined intellectual due to his multifaceted talents and characteristics. He likes to discuss all human knowledge and some of the most vague and unclear difficult problems. I have rarely seen a painter who is as gluttonous for knowledge as he is. There is nothing in poetry and music that he does not want to swallow in one gulp. He is especially infatuated with all the philosophy of painting.

Regarding this point, we can best prove it by quoting his conversation with André Breton. This conversation is published in "The Ideas of a Painter" (Idees dun peintre).

One should intimately understand the inner heart of what one paints. It is meaningless to paint forms for the sake of forms. When I talk to a person, how do I know what kind of form this person is? What I pay attention to is only the expression of his features to me. Only this can give me the impression of life. A person's uniqueness certainly exists. — People who can't hear clearly, no matter how big their earlobes are, it is useless. — Painting cannot exclusively seek likeness. Form must be expressed from the aspect of cultivation. There is nothing to explore outside the features. The same rules apply to animals and plants. The life of a tree is a mystery. No painter can succeed without penetrating its inner heart. Perhaps only Henri Rousseau was ever worried about this. But he still valued the leaves too much, which damaged the whole. We often see in the market people selling a kind of iron wire puzzle, asking people to release a ring from this puzzle. This is exactly the same as the problem of the life of a tree. — Only those who can capture the life of a tree are successful painters. — The problem of the life of inanimate objects is the same. Who can think that he can capture the "movement" of a material? (Immobility is equal to absolute movement). Everything that falls before my senses has its use for me. What is not completely adopted by me must be immature and false....

Grains: Rice Market Continues to Rise Unabated 191

Zhabei: Yesterday, around ten ships arrived from the inland. Market buying interest was somewhat subdued, but inventory along the river was reduced. Sentiment in neighboring markets was extremely positive. Northern粳(jīng) rice prices were firming. The price of medium-grade 粳 rice has risen beyond its level. Dealers' appetite was weak, because they are afraid to buy too much in this unprecedented market situation. However, those with insufficient inventory are defending against further price increases, and are aggressively buying. Therefore, current ordinary medium-grade Zhong-Guan 粳 rice is already reaching 19.5 to 20 yuan. Top-grade 粳 rice is already at the 21 yuan mark. People's livelihood is difficult to the extreme. The trend for Bo-Dao rice is firm, with limited trading. High-quality Yang-Du 籼(xiān) rice is offered at 18 yuan, but no goods have arrived at the port. Various gangs are paying close attention to foreign rice. Therefore, the situation for various 籼 rice is no less than that of 粳 rice. Bai-Yuan rice sales are being watched, and prices are stable.

South Shanghai: Slightly more goods have arrived from the river. Local sales remain brisk. Various Chang-Su-Ji 粳 rice are experiencing continuous price increases due to strong sales. Furthermore, the future supply is uncertain, so the overall market is extremely good. Top-grade rice is offered at around 20 yuan. Bo-Dao rice from Nan-Lu Qing-Jiao and Si-Jing, etc., has not seen development. Buyers are particularly concerned. Prices are similar to the previous market. Customer appetite for Yang 籼 rice is very strong, and sellers are observing the market before selling. The amount of Du-Jian rice stored here is still considerable, and sellers are hoarding to raise prices. Therefore, the overall market for various 籼 rice is rising. Bai-Yuan rice sales are slowly improving. Buyers are urgently requesting goods. Yin-Yuan sales are still slow. The local inventory is considerable, so the market for various Bai-Yuan rice remains mediocre and difficult to prosper in the near term.

Flour Market: Weak Morning, Rebound Afternoon 192

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, prices for various months of foreign wheat reports retreated slightly, about 7-8 jiao. Therefore, speculators in the heat of the market inevitably observed slightly. March, April and May were mostly hovering around the middle, showing a slight weak trend. Deferred months, due to outside long positions, had a slight pull back. Compared with the previous day, it retraced about 1 fen. When the market opened in the afternoon, the near and deferred months rebounded again. It was vaguely heard that the long side did not pay attention to this month because there were only a few days left. The competition for April will inevitably be fierce, with outside short sales exceeding the selling of small and medium factories, while large factories stood by and watched, unwilling to participate in either side. In this situation, if the shorts do not cover, they may eventually be squeezed by the longs, and the irregular market will be created from this. For June, July and August, because large factories did not sell and inland gangs had good intentions, the rebound was very strong. As a result, this month was 2.5 li higher than the previous day, April was 2.5 li lower, June was 7.5 li higher, and May, July and August were 2.5 li higher.
